Prohibition of Maddun al-Farj After Halq: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on maddun al-farj after halq between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits maddun al-farj (sexual activity short of intercourse) after halq, and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Maddun al-farj remains prohibited after halq because it satisfies desire with women; it is deferred until full tahlil.

After halq/taqsir, a pilgrim is partially released from ihram prohibitions. However, the Hanafi school holds that even intimate contact short of intercourse (maddun al-farj) remains unlawful. This lesson examines the Hanafi reasoning and the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on maddun al-farj
After halq, maddun al-farj (kissing, touching with desire) is not permitted. It remains prohibited until complete tahlil (after tawaf al-ziyarah).
This is part of the general rule: 'everything except women' includes all sexual activity with women.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that maddun al-farj is permitted after halq because the exception 'except women' refers only to actual intercourse, not to lesser acts.
Shafi'i restricts the exception to full intercourse.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school argues that maddun al-farj is also a fulfillment of desire with women (قضاء الشهوة بالنساء), so it falls under the same prohibition as intercourse and must be deferred.
The view is based on the prophetic hadith and the principle that anything that gratifies desire with women is included.
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'is may engage in intimate acts (kissing, touching) after halq, while Hanafis must refrain until after tawaf al-ziyarah.
This difference affects the pilgrim's actions during Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
۳۵۶
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
کرنا ہے اور اس مقصد میں حلق اکمل ہے اس لئے بھی حلق ہی افضل ہوگا اور بال کترانے میں اس مقصود میں کچھ نقص ہے یعنی بال کترنے میں مکمل بہ فائی ستھرائی نہیں پائی جاتی ۔ پس یہ نسل اور وضو کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ یعنی جس طرح غسل کرنا وضو سے افضل ہے اسی طرح حلق ، قصر سے افضل ہے۔ اور حلال ہونے کے لئے چوتھائی سر کا منڈانا کافی ہے جیسے وضو میں چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا کافی ہے لیکن پورے سر کا منڈانا اولی ہے کیونکہ اس میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل کی اقتداء ہو جاتی ہے اور تقصیر یعنی کترانا یہ ہے کہ اپنے سر کے بال بقدر انگشت تراش لے۔
ابھی محظورات احرام میں سے فقط عورت حلال نہیں ہوتی
وَقَدْ حَلَ لَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ وَقَالَ مَالِكُ و لا الطيب أيضًا لأنَّهُ مِنْ دَوَاعِى الْجِمَاعِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فيهِ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلِّ شَى إِلَّا النِّسَاءُ وَهُوَ مُقَدَّمُ عَلَى القِيَاسِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الْجِمَاعُ فِيْمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ عِندَنَا خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِي لِأَنَّهُ قَضَاءُ الشَّهْوَةِ بِالنِّسَاءِ فَيُؤَخَرُ إِلَى تَمَامِ الْإِحْلَالِ
ترجمہ اور اس کو سوائے عورتوں کے ہر چیز حلال ہو گئی ۔ اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ سوائے خوشبو کے بھی ۔ کیونکہ وہ جماع کے دوائی میں سے ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضور نوے کا قول اس بارے میں کہ ان کے لئے سوائے عورتوں کے ہر چیز حلال ہو گئی ۔ اور یہ نص قیاس پر مقدم ہے۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک اس کے واسطے مادوان الفرج میں جماع حلال نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی عورتوں کے ساتھ شہوت کو پورا کرنا ہے۔ پس پورے حلال ہونے تک مؤخر کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ حلق یا قصر کے بعد محرم کے لئے ہر وہ چیز حلال ہوگئی جو احرام کی وجہ سے ممنوع ہوگئی تھی ۔ علاوہ عورتوں کے ساتھ جماع اور دوائی جماع کے ۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے جماع کی طرح خوشیوں کا نا بھی حلال نہیں ہوا کیونکہ خوشبو لگا نا دوائر جماع میں سے ہے۔ جیسے عورت کو چھونا اور اس کا بوسہ لین دوائی جماع میں سے ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے حل کے كُلُّ شَىءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءُ یعنی عورتوں کے علاوہ محرم کے لئے ( حلق کے بعد ) ہر چیز حلال ہوگئی ۔ اور یہ ض امام مالک کے پیش کرو قیاس پر مقدم ہے۔ ہمارے نزدیک شرمگاہ کے علاوہ میں بھی جماع حلال نہیں ہوا اگر چہ امام شافعی اس کی حلت کے قائل ہیں ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مادون الفرج میں عورت کے ساتھ جماع کرنا بھی شہوت کو پورا کرنا ہے اس لئے اس کو بھی احلال کے مکمل ہونے یعنی بعد الطواف تک مؤخر کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume three. [The commentary explains:] Shaving (halq) is more complete in achieving the purpose, therefore it is superior. Trimming (qasr) lacks complete purification. This resembles ghusl being superior to wudu. Shaving a quarter of the head suffices for becoming lawful, just as wiping a quarter of the head suffices in wudu, but shaving the whole head is better because it follows the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Taqsir (trimming) is to cut hair to the length of a finger joint. Now, from the prohibitions of ihram, only women are not made lawful. [Arabic text:] "And everything became lawful for him except women." Malik said: "And perfume also, because it is a means to intercourse." Our proof: the Prophet's statement: "Everything became lawful for him except women." This text is given precedence over analogy. And in our view, intercourse short of the private part is not lawful for him, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because it is the gratification of desire with women, so it is deferred until complete exiting of ihram. [Translation of Arabic into Urdu:] And everything became lawful for him except women. Imam Malik said also except perfume, because it is among the means to intercourse. Our proof is the Prophet's statement: for him everything became lawful except women. This text is given precedence over analogy. And in our view, intercourse short of the private part is not lawful; Imam al-Shafi'i differs. Because this also is satisfying desire with women. So it will be deferred until complete exiting. [Commentary continues:] He says that after shaving or trimming, every thing that was prohibited due to ihram becomes lawful for the pilgrim, except intercourse with women and its means. Imam Malik said that perfume also is not lawful, because applying perfume is among the means to intercourse, like touching a woman or kissing her. Our proof is the Prophet's statement: 'everything became lawful except women', and this text is given precedence over Imam Malik's qiyas. In our view, even intercourse short of the private part is not lawful, although Imam al-Shafi'i considers it lawful. Our proof is that intercourse short of the private part with a woman also satisfies desire, so it is deferred until complete exiting, i.e., after tawaf.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding what becomes permissible for a pilgrim after performing halq (shaving) or taqsir (trimming) of the hair. The passage first establishes the Hanafi ruling: all prohibitions of ihram are lifted except for sexual relations with women. Imam Malik adds perfume to the list of still-prohibited items, arguing it is a means to intercourse. The Hanafi response is based on the explicit hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Everything became lawful for him except women.' This text is given priority over qiyas, so perfume is permitted. Then, the text addresses the issue of maddun al-farj (sexual activity short of intercourse). The Hanafi school holds that such activity remains unlawful after halq, only becoming permissible after complete tahlil (which includes tawaf al-ziyarah). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, considering it permissible after halq. The Hanafi reasoning is that such activity also fulfills sexual desire like intercourse itself, so it must be deferred until the final tahlil. The passage thus clarifies the nuanced sequence of exiting ihram, where halq provides partial tahlil but sexual relations remain prohibited until the full ritual is completed.

Key Terms
مادون الفرج (maddun al-farj): Sexual activity short of intercourse, e.g., kissing, touching with desire.
تحلل (tahlil): The state of exiting ihram, becoming permissible to do things previously prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is maddun al-farj prohibited after halq?
A) Because the hadith explicitly mentions it
B) Because it is considered a means to intercourse
C) Because it gratifies desire with women, like intercourse
D) Because the Prophet forbade it separately

Key Takeaway
Maddun al-farj remains prohibited after halq because it also satisfies sexual desire with women; it is deferred until full tahlil.

Stoning the Jamrah Is Not a Cause of Tahlil
Inter-madhhab dispute on ramy as cause of tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that ramy does not cause tahlil and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of jinaayah.

Core Idea
Only a prohibited act (jinaayah) in ihram can cause tahlil; ramy is not prohibited, so it cannot release you.

In the rituals of Hajj, the sequence of acts on Yawm al-Nahr includes ramy, sacrifice, and halq. A key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is whether stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah alone is sufficient to begin exiting ihram. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that tahlil requires a prohibited act, and why ramy does not qualify, as well as the Shafi'i analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: ramy does not cause tahlil; tahlil occurs only through halq/taqsir. The pilgrim remains in ihram after ramy until shaving.
This is the mufta bihi view, based on the principle that only a jinaayah can cause tahlil.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ramy causes partial tahlil. His proof is a qiyas: ramy is specified by Yawm al-Nahr like halq, so it should be analogous to halq in causing tahlil.
Note the use of 'specified by the day' as the common factor.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school refutes the qiyas by pointing out that the effective cause (illah) differs: halq is a prohibited act (jinaayah) in ihram, while ramy is not. The cause of tahlil must be a jinaayah; ramy fails this condition.
This is a classic example of qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference).
4
Examine the objection about tawaf al-ziyarah
An objection is raised: if tawaf al-ziyarah also permits intercourse, then by the same principle it should be a jinaayah. The Hanafi answer is that tawaf does not cause tahlil; tahlil was already achieved by halq. Tawaf merely permits additional acts but is not itself the cause.
This reinforces that tahlil is a single event triggered by halq, not by subsequent acts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Shafi'i pilgrim who has stoned but not shaved is considered partially halal (all except women), while a Hanafi pilgrim must wait until after halq to wear stitched clothes or use perfume.
This affects daily actions during the remaining days of Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رمی احرام سے نکلنے کا سبب ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
ثُمَّ الرَّمَى لَيْسَ مِنْ أَسْبَابِ التَحَلُّلِ عِندَنَا خِلَافَا لِلشَّافِعِي هُوَ يَقُولُ إِنَّهُ يُتَوَفَّتُ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ كَالْحَلْقِ فَيَكُو بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ فِى التَّحْلِيْل وَلَنَا أَنَّ مَا يَكُونَ مُحَلّلًا يَكُونُ جِنَايَةً فِى غَيْراً وَانِهِ كَالْحَلْق وَالرَّمَى لَيْسَ بِحِدَايَةٍ بِخِلَافِ الطَّرَافِ لِأَنَّ التَّحَلَّلَ بِالْحَلِقِ السَّابِقِ لَا بِهِ
ترجمہ پھر رمی جمار ہمارے نزدیک احرام سے نکلنے کے اسباب میں سے نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ برخلاف امام شافی

تشریح امام قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ حلق سے پہلے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرنے سے حاجی احرام سے نہیں نکلتا یعنی ہمارے نزدیک حاجی نے اگر جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کی تو حلال نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ حلق نہ کرائے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فقط رمی جمار کرنے سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کے لئے عورتوں کے علاوہ ہر چیز حلال ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی یوم نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے اور جو چیز یوم نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے وہ محلل یعنی احترام سے نکالنے والی ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے حلق یوم نحر کے ساتھ مؤقت ہے اور محلل ہے پس اسی طرح رمی جمار بھی محلل ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو حلل ہوتی ہے وہ حلال ہونے کے وقت سے پہلے جرم ہوتی ہے جیسے علق احرام کی حالت میں جرم ہے اور رمی جمار جرم نہیں ہے چنانچہ اگر حالت احرام میں کوئی شخص جاکر رمی جمار کرے تو کوئی جرم نہیں پس اس ضابطہ کی وجہ سے رمی جمار محلل نہ ہو گی ۔ بخلاف الطَّواف الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اس ضابطہ کے تحت طواف بھی حالت احترام میں جرم ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ طواف زیارت سے عورتوں کے ساتھ جماع حلال ہوتا ہے پس طواف زیارت محلل ہوا اور بقول آپ کے جو چیز محلل ہوتی ہے وہ حلال ہونے کے وقت سے پہلے جرم ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا طواف احرام کی حالت میں جرم ہونا چاہئے تھا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ طواف زیارت محلل نہیں ہے کیونکہ احرام سے حلال ہونا حلق سے متحقق ہو گیا۔ جو پہلے ہو چکا طواف سے حلال ہونا متفق نہیں ہوا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ عورت کے ساتھ ثبوت پوری کرنے سے پہلے طواف کر لینا چاہئے ۔
Whether ramy (stoning) is a cause of exiting ihram or not, sayings of jurists. [Arabic:] Then, ramy is not among the causes of tahlil in our view, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He says that ramy is specified by the Day of Sacrifice like halq, so it is analogous to halq in causing tahlil. Our [Hanafi] argument is that whatever causes tahlil must be a prohibited act (jinaayah) in ihram, like halq; ramy is not a prohibited act. Unlike tawaf, because tahlil occurred by the preceding halq, not by tawaf. [Translation:] Then, ramy of the jamarat is not among the causes of exiting ihram in our view. There is a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i. [Commentary:] Imam al-Quduri says that if a pilgrim performs ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah before halq, he does not exit ihram; in our view, he does not become halal until he performs halq. Imam al-Shafi'i said that he becomes halal by simply performing ramy, and everything becomes halal for him except women. Shafi'i's proof is that ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah is specified by the Day of Sacrifice, and whatever is specified by the Day of Sacrifice is a cause of tahlil, like halq. Our proof is that whatever causes tahlil must be a prohibited act before tahlil, like halq, and ramy is not a prohibited act. If a person in ihram performs ramy, it is not a violation. Therefore, ramy does not cause tahlil. This is unlike tawaf, which raises a question: According to this principle, tawaf should also be a prohibited act, because tawaf al-ziyarah allows intercourse with women, so it causes tahlil, and according to you, something that causes tahlil must be a prohibited act before tahlil. So why is tawaf not a prohibited act? The answer: Tawaf al-ziyarah does not cause tahlil, because tahlil from ihram is effected by halq, which occurred earlier; tawaf does not cause tahlil. However, it is necessary to perform tawaf before completing sexual relations with women.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether ramy (stoning of the Jamrat al-Aqabah) is a cause of partial tahlil (exiting ihram). The Hanafi position, stated by Imam al-Quduri, is that ramy alone does not cause tahlil; the pilgrim must also perform halq or taqsir. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ramy, like halq, is specified by the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) and therefore causes tahlil. The Hanafi response is based on a principle: whatever causes tahlil must be a prohibited act (jinaayah) within ihram. Halq is prohibited during ihram, so it makes sense that performing it as a ritual brings release. Ramy, however, is not prohibited; it is a prescribed act. Thus it cannot cause tahlil. The passage then addresses an objection: if tawaf al-ziyarah also causes release from the prohibition of intercourse, then by the same logic it should be a prohibited act. The Hanafi answer is that tawaf al-ziyarah does not actually cause tahlil; the release from ihram occurs via halq, and tawaf merely permits intercourse with women, but does not itself cause tahlil. Thus, the principle is consistent: only acts that are themselves prohibited in ihram (like halq) can be causes of tahlil.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): Stoning the jamarat (pillars) during Hajj, specifically Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr.
تحلل (tahlil): The act of exiting ihram and becoming permissible to do previously prohibited things.
جناية (jinaayah): A prohibited act in ihram that incurs a penalty (dam or fidyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following acts is a necessary cause for partial tahlil (exiting ihram) after performing ramy?
A) Performing tawaf al-ziyarah
B) Shaving or trimming the hair (halq/taqsir)
C) Sacrificing an animal (damm)
D) Stoning the other two jamarat

Key Takeaway
Ramy does not cause tahlil in the Hanafi school; only a prohibited act (jinaayah) like halq can release the pilgrim from ihram.

Timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
States the timing and evidence for tawaf al-ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid days for performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah according to the Hanafi school and identify the dalil for its timing.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is valid on any of the three Days of Sacrifice, not only Yawm al-Nahr.

After completing rami, halq, and dhabh in Mina, the pilgrim proceeds to Makkah for Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The classical Hanafi text of al-Quduri specifies a window of three days for this pillar of Hajj, supported by the action of the Prophet ﷺ and a Quranic link between sacrifice and tawaf. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, not merely a wajib. Its omission invalidates the Hajj.
Hanafi school: arkan are essential; missing them makes the act batil.
2
State the permissible days
The text states it may be performed on the same day (Yawm al-Nahr, 10th Dhul-Hijjah), the next day (11th), or the day after (12th). These three days are called Ayyam al-Nahr.
The 13th is not included; tawaf after Ayyam al-Nahr requires a dam for delay.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The Prophet ﷺ shaved (halq) then proceeded to Makkah, performed tawaf, returned to Mina, and prayed Zuhr. This establishes the practice on Yawm al-Nahr.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but suffices for a ruling of this nature.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
Allah mentions tawaf immediately after sacrifice (Quran 22:29), indicating that the time for tawaf is linked to the days of sacrifice.
The verse: 'Then let them complete their rites and perform their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House.' The context includes sacrifice.

قَالَ ثُمَّ يَأْتِى مِنَ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ مَكَّةَ أو مِنَ الْعَد  َأوْ مِنْ بَعدِ الغَدِ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ طَوافِ الزِّيَارَةِ سَبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطِ لِمَا رُوى أَنَّ النَّى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمَّا حَلَقَ أَفَاضَ إِلى مَكَّة فطاف بالبيتِ ثُمَّ عَادَ إِلَى مِنِى وَصَلَّى الظَّهْرَ بِمِنى
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا پھر مکہ میں آئے اسی دن یا گیارہویں کو یا بار ہوئیں کو پس خانہ کعبہ کا طواف کرے طواف زیارت سات پھیرے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب سر منڈایا تو مکہ تشریف لائے ۔ پھر بیت اللہ کا طواف کیا ، پھر منی کو واپس آئے اور منی میں ظہر کی نماز پڑھی۔
تشریح فرمایا کہ یوم نحر کومنٹی میں رمی ، حلق اور ذبیح کے بعد اسی دن مکتہ المکرمہ آجائے یا گیارہویں کو یا بارہویں کو۔ پھر بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے۔ اس طواف کا نام طواف زیارت ہے اور حج کے ارکان میں سے ایک رکن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی حلق کرایا پھر مکہ میں آکر بیت اللہ کا طواف کیا پھر منی کو تشریف لے گئے اور منی میں ظہر کی نماز ادا کی۔
طواف زیارت کا وقت ایام النحر ہیں
وَوَقْته أَيَّامُ النَّحْرُ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عَطَفَ الطَّوَافَ عَلَى الذَّبْحِ قَالَ فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا ثُمَّ قَالَ ﴿وَلَيَطْوَفُوا فَكَانَ
[Al-Quduri] said: Then he comes from that day to Makkah, or on the next day, or after the next day, and performs tawaf around the House, the Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he shaved, he went to Makkah, performed tawaf around the House, then returned to Mina and prayed Zuhr in Mina. [Translation:] Al-Quduri said: Then he comes to Makkah on that day (Yawm al-Nahr) or on the 11th or 12th, then performs tawaf of the Kaaba, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits. Because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he shaved his head, went to Makkah, performed tawaf, then returned to Mina and prayed Zuhr in Mina. [Commentary:] He said: On Yawm al-Nahr, after performing rami, halq, and dhabh in Mina, he should come to Makkah on that day, or on the 11th, or on the 12th. Then he should perform tawaf. This tawaf is called Tawaf al-Ziyarah and is one of the pillars (arkan) of Hajj. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) also shaved, then came to Makkah, performed tawaf, then went to Mina and prayed Zuhr there. The time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the Days of Sacrifice (Ayyam al-Nahr). [Arabic:] And its time is the Days of Sacrifice, because Allah Almighty connected tawaf to slaughter, saying: 'So eat from them' then He said: 'And let them perform tawaf' so it was...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam al-Quduri regarding the timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. The ruling states that after performing ramy, halq, and sacrifice in Mina on Yawm al-Nahr, the pilgrim proceeds to Makkah to perform tawaf of the Kaaba, seven circuits. This may be done on the same day (Yawm al-Nahr), the following day (11th), or the day after (12th). The proof is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved, went to Makkah, performed tawaf, returned to Mina, and prayed Zuhr there. The passage also notes that the time for this tawaf is the Days of Sacrifice (Ayyam al-Nahr), as indicated by the Quranic verse where tawaf is mentioned after sacrifice (Quran 22:29). This establishes that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a distinct obligation performed within a specific window.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed during Hajj after coming from Mina; also called tawaf al-ifadah.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The Days of Sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah.

D) 13th of Dhul-Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a pillar of Hajj, must be performed within Ayyam al-Nahr (10th–12th Dhul-Hijjah); delay beyond requires a dam but the tawaf remains valid.

The Requirement of Jurm for Tahallul: Ramy vs. Halq
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i claim that ramy alone causes tahallul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that a muhill must be a jurm and apply it to distinguish ramy and halq in tahallul.

Core Idea
Only a prohibited act (jurm) in ihram can cause tahallul; ramy is permissible, so it cannot.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i claim that stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba alone suffices to exit ihram. The core of the dispute is the logical principle (dalil aqli) that the cause of tahallul must be a crime (jurm) in the state of ihram. Let's walk through the arguments step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that for the Hanafi school, ramy does not cause tahallul; halq (shaving) is required. The pilgrim remains in ihram until halq is performed.
Imam al-Quduri's matn explicitly states this.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ramy alone causes tahallul (except for marital relations). His proof is qiyas: ramy is time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr like halq, so it should also be muhill.
The Shafi'i argument relies on time-specificity as the illa.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on a rational principle: a muhill must be a jurm (prohibited act) in the state of ihram before the time of halal. Shaving is a jurm (prohibited in ihram), so it qualifies. Ramy is permissible in ihram (not a jurm), so it cannot be muhill.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof), not naqli.
4
Address the tawaf objection
An objection is raised: tawaf al-ziyarah permits women, so it seems to be muhill, yet tawaf is not a jurm. The Hanafi response: tawaf is not actually muhill; tahallul is achieved solely through halq. Tawaf is only a condition for permitting marital relations, not a cause of exit.
This reinforces the principle: only jurm can be muhill.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafi, the pilgrim must perform ramy then halq to become halal; according to Shafi'i, ramy alone suffices (except for women). This affects when the pilgrim can engage in previously prohibited acts.
Both positions are well-established within their respective schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج کے وہ فرماتے ہیں رمی بھی سر منڈانے کے مانند یوم نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے پس رمی بھی حلال کرنے میں بمنزلہ حلق کے ہوگی ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو چیز احرام سے حلال کرنے والی ہے وہ حلال ہونے سے پہلے جرم ہوتی ہے جیسے سر کا منڈانا اور رمی جمار جرم نہیں ہے بر خلاف طواف کے کیونکہ حلال ہونا طلق سابق کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ طواف کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح امام قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ حلق سے پہلے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرنے سے حاجی احرام سے نہیں نکلتا یعنی ہمارے نزدیک حاجی نے اگر جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کی تو حلال نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ حلق نہ کرائے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ فقط رمی جمار کرنے سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کے لئے عورتوں کے علاوہ ہر چیز حلال ہو جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی یوم نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے اور جو چیز یوم نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے وہ محلل یعنی احترام سے نکالنے والی ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے حلق یوم نحر کے ساتھ مؤقت ہے اور محلل ہے پس اسی طرح رمی جمار بھی محلل ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو حلل ہوتی ہے وہ حلال ہونے کے وقت سے پہلے جرم ہوتی ہے جیسے علق احرام کی حالت میں جرم ہے اور رمی جمار جرم نہیں ہے چنانچہ اگر حالت احرام میں کوئی شخص جاکر رمی جمار کرے تو کوئی جرم نہیں پس اس ضابطہ کی وجہ سے رمی جمار محلل نہ ہو گی ۔ بخلاف الطَّواف الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اس ضابطہ کے تحت طواف بھی حالت احترام میں جرم ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ طواف زیارت سے عورتوں کے ساتھ جماع حلال ہوتا ہے پس طواف زیارت محلل ہوا اور بقول آپ کے جو چیز محلل ہوتی ہے وہ حلال ہونے کے وقت سے پہلے جرم ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا طواف احرام کی حالت میں جرم ہونا چاہئے تھا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ طواف زیارت محلل نہیں ہے کیونکہ احرام سے حلال ہونا حلق سے متحقق ہو گیا۔ جو پہلے ہو چکا طواف سے حلال ہونا متفق نہیں ہوا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ عورت کے ساتھ ثبوت پوری کرنے سے پہلے طواف کر لینا چاہئے ۔
He (Al-Quduri) says: Ramy (stoning) is also like head-shaving, time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr, so ramy is also like halq in causing halal (exit from ihram). Our proof is: That which causes exit from ihram is a crime (jurm) before exit, like head-shaving. Ramy al-Jimar (stoning the pebbles) is not a crime, unlike tawaf, because exit is due to previous halal, not due to tawaf. Explanation: Imam Al-Quduri says: By stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba before halq, the pilgrim does not exit ihram; that is, in our view, if the pilgrim stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba, he will not be halal until he shaves. Imam al-Shafi'i said: By only ramy al-jimar, he will become halal, and for him everything except women becomes halal. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: Ramy Jamrat al-Aqaba is time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr, and what is time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr is muhill (cause of exit), like halq is time-specific and muhill, so similarly ramy al-jimar is muhill. Our proof: That which causes halal (exit) is a crime before the time of exit, like shaving is a crime in the state of ihram, and ramy al-jimar is not a crime; similarly, if in the state of ihram someone goes and performs ramy al-jimar, it is not a crime, so due to this principle, ramy al-jimar is not muhill. This is the answer to an objection from a question regarding tawaf. The question: According to this principle, tawaf should also be a crime in the state of ihram because tawaf al-ziyarah makes marital relations halal, so tawaf al-ziyarah is muhill, and according to you, what is muhill is a crime before the time of halal. Therefore, tawaf should be a crime in the state of ihram, but it is not. The answer: Tawaf al-ziyarah is not muhill, because exit from ihrm occurs through halq, which has already happened, so exit is not achieved through tawaf. However, it is necessary that he perform tawaf before completing the relationship with his wife.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether stoning the Jamarat (ramy) alone can cause a pilgrim to exit the state of ihram (tahallul). The Hanafi position, as stated by Imam al-Quduri and explained by the commentator, is that ramy does not effect tahallul; rather, the pilgrim remains in ihram until he performs halq (shaving or trimming the hair). The Shafi'i position, on the other hand, holds that ramy alone is sufficient for tahallul (except for marital relations). The text then provides the proofs for both schools. The Shafi'i proof relies on qiyas: since ramy is time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr just like halq, it should also be a cause of tahallul. The Hanafi proof is based on a rational principle: an act that causes tahallul must be a prohibited act (jurm) in the state of ihram. Shaving hair is prohibited in ihram, so it is a jurm and thus muhill. Stoning, however, is permissible in ihram, so it is not a jurm and cannot be muhill. An objection is then raised: tawaf al-ziyarah (the circumambulation of visit) permits women, so it should also be considered muhill and thus a jurm, but it is not prohibited in ihram. The Hanafi response clarifies that tawaf is not actually muhill; tahallul is achieved solely through halq. Tawaf is only a condition for permitting marital relations, but it does not constitute exit from ihram. Therefore, the principle holds: only a jurm (like halq) can be muhill.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): Stoning the Jamarat (specifically Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr) in Hajj.
حلق (halq): Shaving or trimming the hair of the head, performed after ramy on Yawm al-Nahr.
محلل (muhill): Something that causes tahallul (exit from ihram) and makes permissible what was prohibited.
جرم (jurm): A prohibited act in the state of ihram, like shaving hair or hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that ramy al-jimar does not cause tahallul?
A) Because ramy is not time-specific to Yawm al-Nahr
B) Because ramy is not a jurm (crime) in the state of ihram
C) Because ramy must be performed after halq
D) Because ramy is only for men

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only an act that is prohibited (jurm) in ihram, such as halq, can cause tahallul; ramy, being permissible, does not.

Time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Establishing the time for tawaf al-ziyarah from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for tawaf al-ziyarah according to the Hanafi school and explain the Quranic proof using the principle of 'atf (conjunction).

Core Idea
Tawaf al-ziyarah shares the time of sacrifice via Quranic conjunction; its earliest time is after dawn of the 10th.

This lesson examines the time for tawaf al-ziyarah, a pillar of Hajj. The Hanafi school derives its time from the Quranic conjunction of tawaf with sacrifice, supported by the Prophet's practice. Understanding this time ensures the pilgrim performs the rite in its preferred period without unnecessary delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that tawaf al-ziyarah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, obligatory (fard 'ayn) to perform. Its proper time is the Days of Sacrifice.
The text explicitly calls it a rukn.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse (Surah al-Hajj 22:28-29) where 'tawaf' is conjoined to 'sacrifice' by 'thumma' (then), indicating shared timing.
The conjunction (عطف) implies time equality.
3
Understand the linguistic argument
Apply the Hanafi principle that the conjoined and conjoiner share the same time. Both sacrifice and tawaf become obligatory in the same window.
This is a clear 'dalala' from the Quran.
4
Determine the earliest and preferred time
The earliest is after dawn of Yawm al-Nahr because before that is Wuquf. The first day is most virtuous, like sacrifice.
This is based on sequential ordering: Wuquf precedes tawaf.
5
Note the mufta bihi and cross-school difference
The Hanafi position is that tawaf is restricted to these three days; performance after is valid but disliked. Other schools may allow later without dislike.
Know the practical difference for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یوم النحر کے دن منی میں رمی ، حلق اور ذبح کے بعد مکہ مکرمہ آجائے قَالَ ثُمَّ يَأْتِى مِنَ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ مَكَّةَ أو مِنَ الْعَد  َأوْ مِنْ بَعدِ الغَدِ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ طَوافِ الزِّيَارَةِ سَبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطِ لِمَا رُوى أَنَّ النَّى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمَّا حَلَقَ أَفَاضَ إِلى مَكَّة فطاف بالبيتِ ثُمَّ عَادَ إِلَى مِنِى وَصَلَّى الظَّهْرَ بِمِنى تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ یوم نحر کو منی میں رمی حلق اور ذبیح کے بعد اسی دن مکتہ المکرمہ آجائے یا گیارہویں کو یا بارہویں کو۔ پھر بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے۔ اس طواف کا نام طواف زیارت ہے اور حج کے ارکان میں سے ایک رکن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی حلق کرایا پھر مکہ میں آکر بیت اللہ کا طواف کیا پھر منی کو تشریف لے گئے اور منی میں ظہر کی نماز ادا کی۔ طواف زیارت کا وقت ایام النحر ہیں وَوَقْته أَيَّامُ النَّحْرُ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى عَطَفَ الطَّوَافَ عَلَى الذَّبْحِ قَالَ فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا ثُمَّ قَالَ ﴿وَلَيَطْوُفُوا فَكَانَ وَقْتُهُمَا وَاحِدًا وَأَوَّلُ وَقَتِهِ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ لاَنَّ مَا قَبْلَهُ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ وَقْتِ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالطَّوَافَ مَرَتَبٌ عَلَيْهِ وَأفْضَلُ هذهِ الأَيَّامِ أَوَّلُهَا كَمَا فِى التَّضْحِيَّةِ وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ أَفْضَلُهَا أَوَّلُهَا تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ طواف زیارت کا وقت قربانی کے دن ہیں یعنی دسویں، گیارہویں، بارہویں ذی الحجہ ۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ ثُمَّ ليَقْضُوا تَفَتهُمْ وَلَيُوفُوا نذورَهُمْ وَليَطوفُوا بالبيت العتيق - (المج: ۲۹، ۲۸) میں طواف کو قربانی کرنے پر معطوف کیا گیا ہے اور معطوف اور معطوف علیہ دونوں کا وقت ایک ہوتا ہے اس لئے قربانی اور طواف زیارت دونوں کا ایک وقت ہو گا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ قربانی ان ایام کے بعد جائز نہیں اور طواف ان ایام کے بعد بھی مع الکراہت مشروع ہے اور طواف کا اقل وقت یوم نحر کی فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ طلوع فجر سے پہلے رات کا وقت تو وقوف عرفہ کا وقت ہے اور طواف وقوف پر مرتب ہے ۔ یعنی وقوف کے وقت کے بعد طواف کا وقت ہے۔ اور وقوف کا وقت یوم نحر کی طلوع فجر تک رہتا ہے لہذا طلوع فجر کے بعد سے طواف کا وقت شروع ہو جائے گا البتہ ان ایام میں سے پہلا دن طواف زیارت کے لئے افضل ہے۔ جیسے انہیں ایام میں سے پہلا دن قربانی کے لئے افضل ہے اور حدیث میں بھی یہ ہے کہ ان ایام میں افضل پہلا دن ہے۔
On the day of Yawm al-Nahr, after ramy, halq, and dhabh in Mina, come to Makkah al-Mukarramah. He (Al-Quduri) said: Then he comes on that same day to Makkah, or on the second day, or on the day after the second, and performs tawaf of the House, tawaf al-ziyarah, seven circuits, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him), when he shaved, he went to Makkah and performed tawaf of the House, then returned to Mina and prayed Zuhr in Mina. Explanation: Imam Al-Quduri says: After ramy, halq, and dhabh in Mina on Yawm al-Nahr, he comes to Makkah al-Mukarramah on the same day, or on the 11th, or on the 12th. Then he performs tawaf of the House of Allah. This tawaf is called tawaf al-ziyarah and it is one of the pillars of Hajj. The proof is that the Prophet (SAW) also shaved, then came to Makkah and performed tawaf of the House, then went to Mina and performed Zuhr prayer in Mina. The time of tawaf al-ziyarah is the Days of Sacrifice. And its time is the Days of Sacrifice because Allah Most High conjoined tawaf upon dhabh (sacrifice). He said: 'Then eat thereof and feed the poor unfortunate' then He said: 'and let them perform tawaf of the Ancient House.' So the time of both is one. And the earliest time for it is after dawn of Yawm al-Nahr because what is before that of the night is the time of standing at Arafah, and tawaf is sequential upon it. And the most virtuous of these days is the first, as in the sacrifice. And in the hadith: 'The most virtuous of them is the first.' Explanation: Imam Al-Quduri said: The time of tawaf al-ziyarah is the days of sacrifice, i.e., the 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul Hijjah. Because the words of Allah: 'Then eat thereof and feed the poor unfortunate, then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and perform tawaf of the Ancient House' (Surah al-Hajj 22:28-29) conjoin tawaf upon sacrifice, and the conjoined and the conjoiner both have the same time. Therefore, sacrifice and tawaf al-ziyarah both have the same time. However, it is necessary that sacrifice is not permissible after these days, while tawaf after these days is still permissible but with dislike (karahah). The minimum time for tawaf begins after dawn of Yawm al-Nahr because before dawn, the night is the time of Wuquf at Arafah, and tawaf is sequential upon it. That is, after the time of Wuquf comes the time of tawaf. The time of Wuquf continues until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr, so after dawn, the time of tawaf begins. However, the first of these days is most virtuous for tawaf al-ziyarah, just as the first of these days is most virtuous for sacrifice. And in the hadith: 'The most virtuous of them is the first.'
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the time for tawaf al-ziyarah (the circumambulation of visit), which is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. The author establishes that its time is the Days of Sacrifice (Ayyam al-Nahr), meaning the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah. The proof is from the Quranic verse where Allah conjoins tawaf with sacrifice (dhabh), indicating that both share the same time. Additionally, the Sunnah of the Prophet (SAW) is cited: after shaving on Yawm al-Nahr, he went to Makkah and performed tawaf, then returned to Mina. The earliest time for tawaf al-ziyarah begins after dawn (fajr) of Yawm al-Nahr, because the night before is reserved for the standing at Arafah. After the time for Wuquf ends at dawn, the time for tawaf begins. The first day (Yawm al-Nahr) is the most virtuous, as is the case with sacrifice. However, it is important to note that while sacrifice is not valid after the Days of Sacrifice, tawaf al-ziyarah may be performed after these days with dislike (karahah).

Key Terms
طواف زیارت (tawaf al-ziyarah): The circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after ramy, halq, and dhabh on the Days of Sacrifice, a rukn of Hajj.
ایام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The Days of Sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf 'arafah): The standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the earliest time for tawaf al-ziyarah according to the Hanafi school?
A) After sunset of Yawm al-Nahr
B) After dawn of Yawm al-Nahr
C) After Zuhr of Yawm al-Nahr
D) After completing all other rites

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-ziyarah must be performed during the Days of Sacrifice; the earliest time is after dawn on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Raml and Sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling with conditional scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether raml and sa'y are performed in tawaf al-ziyarah based on prior sa'y performance, and explain the rationale that each is only prescribed once.

Core Idea
Raml and sa'y are each performed only once in Hajj — if sa'y was done earlier, neither is repeated in tawaf al-ziyarah.

You have learned about tawaf al-qudoom and tawaf al-ziyarah as key circumambulations in Hajj. This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific question: should the pilgrim perform raml and sa'y in tawaf al-ziyarah? The answer depends on whether the pilgrim already performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudoom. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary duplication of rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The ruling depends on whether the pilgrim performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah after tawaf al-qudoom. This is the key variable.
2
Scenario A: Sa'y already done
If the pilgrim performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudoom, then in tawaf al-ziyarah he does not perform raml, and he does not perform sa'y again.
Because sa'y is wajib only once, and raml is only in a tawaf followed by sa'y.
3
Scenario B: No prior sa'y
If the pilgrim did not perform sa'y earlier, then in tawaf al-ziyarah he performs raml and then performs sa'y after this tawaf.
This fulfills the one required sa'y and the sunnah raml.
4
Trace the rationale
Both sa'y and raml are prescribed only once in Hajj. Raml is legislated only in a tawaf that is followed by sa'y. Therefore, they cannot be repeated.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that each ritual has a single occasion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَاءِ وَالْمَرْوَةِ عَقِيبَ طَوافِ الْقُدُوم لَمْ يَرْمُلُ فِى  َهذَا الطَّوافِ وَلَا سَعَى عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَمُ يُقَدِّمُ السَّعْيَ رَمَلَ فِى هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَسَعَى بَعْدَهُ لانَّ السَّعَى لَمْ يَشْرَعُ الامَرَّةَ وَالرَّمْلُ مَا شُرعَ الَّامَرَّةً فِي طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعَى ترجمہ اگر طواف قدوم کے بعد صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کر چکا ہو تو اس طواف زیارت میں رمل نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اس پر سعی بھی نہیں ہے اور اگر صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان پہلے سعی نہیں کی تو اس طواف میں رمل کرے اور اس کے بعد سعی کرے کیونکہ سبھی مشروع نہیں ہوئی مگر ایک بار اور رمل مشروع نہیں ہوا مگر ایک بار ایسے طواف میں جس کے بعد سعی ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی طواف قدوم کے بعد اگر سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کر چکا ہو تو طواف زیارت میں رمل نہیں کرے گا اور اس پر سبھی بھی واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر پہلے سعی بین الصفا والمروہ نہیں کی تو اس طواف میں رمل کرے اور اس کے بعد سعی بھی کرے۔ کیونکہ سعی بھی انتہ ایک مرتبہ مشروع ہوئی ہے اور رمل بھی ایک ہی مرتبہ ایسے طواف کے بعد مشروع ہوا ہے جس کے بعد سعی ہو۔
So if he performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah after tawaf al-qudoom, he does not perform raml in this tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah) and there is no sa'y upon him. And if he did not perform sa'y earlier, he performs raml in this tawaf and performs sa'y after it, because sa'y is not prescribed except once, and raml is not prescribed except once in a tawaf after which there is sa'y. Translation: If after tawaf al-qudoom he performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then in this tawaf al-ziyarah he will not perform raml, and there is no sa'y upon him. And if he did not perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah earlier, then in this tawaf he performs raml and after it he performs sa'y, because sa'y is only prescribed once, and raml is only prescribed once, in a tawaf after which there is sa'y. Explanation: The issue is that if the pilgrim has performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah after tawaf al-qudoom, then in tawaf al-ziyarah he will not perform raml and sa'y is not obligatory upon him. And if he did not perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah earlier, then in this tawaf he performs raml and after it he also performs sa'y, because sa'y is only prescribed once, and raml is also prescribed only once after a tawaf which is followed by sa'y.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on whether raml (brisk walking with shoulder movements) and sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah) are to be performed in tawaf al-ziyarah. The ruling depends on whether the pilgrim had already performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudoom (arrival circumambulation). According to the Hanafi school, sa'y is prescribed only once in Hajj, and raml is prescribed only once, in a tawaf after which sa'y is performed. Therefore, if the pilgrim already performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudoom, then in tawaf al-ziyarah, raml is not done (since raml is tied to a tawaf that is followed by sa'y), and separate sa'y is not required because it was already done. If the pilgrim did not perform sa'y earlier, then in tawaf al-ziyarah, raml is performed, and sa'y is performed after this tawaf. The reasoning is that both actions are only legislated once per Hajj. This is a practical ruling for pilgrims to avoid duplication.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Walking quickly with short steps and slight shoulder movement during tawaf, prescribed for the first three circuits.
سعی (sa'y): The act of walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah, a wajib ritual in Hajj and Umrah.
طواف قدوم (tawaf al-qudoom): The circumambulation of arrival performed upon entering Makkah for Hajj, a sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudoom, what should he do during tawaf al-ziyarah?
A) Perform raml in tawaf and sa'y afterward
B) Perform raml only, no sa'y
C) Neither raml nor sa'y are performed
D) Perform sa'y only, no raml

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sa'y is performed only once in Hajj, and raml only in a tawaf followed by sa'y; thus tawaf al-ziyarah requires neither if sa'y was already done after tawaf al-qudoom.

Time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Its Virtue
Figh ruling with proof from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah according to the Hanafi school, derive it from the Quranic proof, and identify the best day for its performance.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah shares the same time as sacrifice: the Days of Nahr.

When must a pilgrim perform the essential Tawaf al-Ziyarah? Is it limited to the Day of Nahr, or can it be delayed? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling based on the Quranic conjunction of tawaf with sacrifice, and explains the preferred timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah), which is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. The focus is on its time: within which days must it be performed?
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is fard, but the time is a separate ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 22:28-29, where Allah says 'then let them complete their rites... and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House.' The conjunction (waw) links tawaf to sacrifice.
Hanafi usul: the ma'tuf (tawaf) shares the time of ma'tuf 'alayh (sacrifice).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'wal yattawwafu' is conjoined to the context of sacrifice. The Hanafi principle is that the conjunction (عطف) implies co-temporality unless there is evidence otherwise.
Sacrifice is performed on the Days of Nahr (10th-12th). Hence tawaf also falls in those days.
4
Specify the earliest time
The earliest time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah is after Fajr on the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr). Before Fajr is reserved for standing at Arafah, which precedes tawaf in sequence.
The night of the 10th is still Woquf time; tawaf comes after.
5
Note the virtue and ikhtilaf
The first day (10th) is the most virtuous, like sacrifice. Some schools, e.g. Shafi'i, allow it after midnight of the 10th. Hanafis require Fajr. The tawaf can be delayed up to the 12th, but delay beyond incurs dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah) and requires dam.
Practical difference: a pilgrim arriving after Fajr on 10th can do tawaf immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
وَقْتُهُمَا وَاحِدًا وَأَوَّلُ وَقَتِهِ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ لاَنَّ مَا قَبْلَهُ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ وَقْتِ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالطَّوَافَ مَرَتَبٌ عَلَيْهِ وَأفْضَلُ هذهِ الأَيَّامِ أَوَّلُهَا كَمَا فِى التَّضْحِيَّةِ وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ أَفْضَلُهَا أَوَّلُهَا
ترجمہ اور طواف کا وقت قربانی کے ایام ہیں۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے قربانی پر طواف کا عطف کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا فكلوا منھا پھر کہا، وليطوفوا پس ان دونوں کا ایک وقت ہوگا۔ اور طواف زیارت کا ابتدائی وقت یوم نحر کی فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد ہے کیونکہ طلوع فجر سے پہلے رات کا وقت تو وقوف عرفہ کا وقت ہے اور طواف اس پر مرتب ہے اور ان ایام میں پہلا دن افضل ہے جیسا کہ قربانی میں ہے اور حدیث میں ہے کہ ان ایام میں افضل پہلا دن ہے۔
تشریح امام قدوری نے فرمایا کہ طواف زیارت کا وقت قربانی کے دن ہیں یعنی دسویں، گیارہویں، بارہویں ذی الحجہ ۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ ثُمَّ ليَقْضُوا تَفَتهُمْ وَلَيُوفُوا نذورَهُمْ وَليَطوفُوا بالبيت العتيق - (المج: ۲۹، ۲۸) میں طواف کو قربانی کرنے پر معطوف کیا گیا ہے اور معطوف اور معطوف علیہ دونوں کا وقت ایک ہوتا ہے اس لئے قربانی اور طواف زیارت دونوں کا ایک وقت ہو گا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ قربانی ان ایام کے بعد جائز نہیں اور طواف ان ایام کے بعد بھی مع الکراہت مشروع ہے اور طواف کا اقل وقت یوم نحر کی فجر طلوع ہونے کے بعد سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ طلوع فجر سے پہلے رات کا وقت تو وقوف عرفہ کا وقت ہے اور طواف وقوف پر مرتب ہے ۔ یعنی وقوف کے وقت کے بعد طواف کا وقت ہے۔ اور وقوف کا وقت یوم نحر کی طلوع فجر تک رہتا ہے لہذا طلوع فجر کے بعد سے طواف کا وقت شروع ہو جائے گا البتہ ان ایام میں سے پہلا دن طواف زیارت کے لئے افضل ہے۔ جیسے انہیں ایام میں سے پہلا دن قربانی کے لئے افضل ہے اور حدیث میں بھی یہ ہے کہ ان ایام میں افضل پہلا دن ہے۔
Book of Hajj. Their time is one, and the beginning of its time is after the dawn of the Day of Nahr, because what is before it of the night is the time of standing at Arafah, and the tawaf is arranged after it. And the best of these days is the first of them, as in the sacrifice. And in the hadith: The best of them is the first of them.
Translation: And the time of tawaf is the days of sacrifice. Because Allah Most High has coordinated tawaf with sacrifice. Thus He said: 'So eat of them' then He said 'and let them perform tawaf.' So both have the same time. And the initial time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is after the dawn of the Day of Nahr, because the night before dawn is the time of standing at Arafah, and tawaf is arranged after it. And among these days, the first day is best, as in the sacrifice. And in the hadith: Among these days, the best is the first day.
Commentary: Imam al-Quduri said that the time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the days of sacrifice, i.e., the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah. Because in the saying of Allah Most High: 'So eat of them and feed the distressed poor, then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' (al-Hajj 22:28-29), tawaf is coordinated with sacrifice, and the coordinated and the coordinator have one time. So sacrifice and Tawaf al-Ziyarah have one time. However, it is necessary that sacrifice is not permissible after these days, while tawaf after these days is still prescribed but with dislike. And the minimum time of tawaf begins after the dawn of the Day of Nahr. Because the night before dawn is the time of standing at Arafah, and tawaf is arranged after standing. That is, the time of tawaf is after the time of standing. And the time of standing lasts until the dawn of the Day of Nahr, so after dawn the time of tawaf begins. However, among these days, the first day is best for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, just as the first day is best for sacrifice. And the hadith also says that the best of these days is the first day.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). The author, Imam al-Quduri, states that the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the Days of Nahr (10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah). The proof is from the Quran where Allah coordinates tawaf with sacrifice (wa li-yattawwafu), and since the coordinated and coordinator share the same time, the tawaf time is the same as the sacrifice time. However, a key difference is that sacrifice is not valid after these days, while tawaf is still valid but disliked (makruh). The earliest time for this tawaf is after Fajr on the 10th, because before Fajr is the time for standing at Arafah, and tawaf comes after standing. The best day among these is the first day, as supported by hadith. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj and its time is specified, though delaying it beyond the Days of Nahr incurs a dam.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The tawaf performed after returning from Mina on the Day of Nahr; it is the fard tawaf of Hajj.
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.
وقوف بعرفة (Woquf bi-Arafah): Standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; it is a rukn of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah begin according to the Hanafi school?
A) After midnight on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah
B) After Fajr on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah
C) After Zuhr on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah
D) After the sun sets on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is valid from after Fajr on the 10th till sunset on the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah; performing it on the 10th is most virtuous.

Ramal and Sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah: A Conditional Ruling
Conditional ruling on ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for performing ramal and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and apply the ruling to a pilgrim's timeline.

Core Idea
Sa'y and ramal are prescribed only once; Tawaf al-Ziyarah repeats them only if sa'y was not done earlier.

The passage clarifies a common point of confusion in Hajj: whether a pilgrim must perform ramal (quick walking) and sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah) during Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the tawaf of the day of sacrifice). The answer depends entirely on whether he already performed sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf). This lesson unpacks the conditional ruling and the underlying reasoning that both acts are prescribed only once.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The pilgrim either performed sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum, or he did not. These are the only two possibilities covered by the text.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If sa'y was done after Tawaf al-Qudum: no ramal and no sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If sa'y was not done: perform ramal in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and then sa'y after it.
The sequence matters: ramal is done during the tawaf (first three rounds), sa'y follows the tawaf.
3
Explain the legal reasoning (talil)
The text states that sa'y is prescribed only once, and ramal is prescribed only once in a tawaf that is followed by sa'y. Since the pilgrim already performed sa'y (or not), the ruling follows accordingly.
This is a form of ta'lil: the reason (illa) is the once-only prescription.
4
Apply to the pilgrim's timeline
Trace from arrival: Tawaf al-Qudum → optional sa'y. If sa'y was done, Tawaf al-Ziyarah has no ramal and no sa'y. If sa'y was delayed, Tawaf al-Ziyarah includes ramal and sa'y.
This ensures the pilgrim does not repeat the wajib sa'y unnecessarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَاءِ وَالْمَرْوَةِ عَقِيبَ طَوافِ الْقُدُوم لَمْ يَرْمُلُ فِى هَذَا الطَّوافِ وَلَا سَعَى عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَمُ يُقَدِّمُ السَّعْيَ رَمَلَ فِى هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَسَعَى بَعْدَهُ لانَّ السَّعَى لَمْ يَشْرَعُ الامَرَّةَ وَالرَّمْلُ مَا شُرعَ الَّامَرَّةً فِي طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعَى
ترجمہ اگر طواف قدوم کے بعد صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کر چکا ہو تو اس طواف زیارت میں رمل نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اس پر سعی بھی نہیں ہے اور اگر صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان پہلے سعی نہیں کی تو اس طواف میں رمل کرے اور اس کے بعد سعی کرے کیونکہ سبھی مشروع نہیں ہوئی مگر ایک بار اور رمل مشروع نہیں ہوا مگر ایک بار ایسے طواف میں جس کے بعد سعی ہو۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حاجی طواف قدوم کے بعد اگر سعی بین الصفا والمروہ کر چکا ہو تو طواف زیارت میں رمل نہیں کرے گا اور اس پر سبھی بھی واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر پہلے سعی بین الصفا والمروہ نہیں کی تو اس طواف میں رمل کرے اور اس کے بعد سعی بھی کرے۔ کیونکہ سعی بھی انتہ ایک مرتبہ مشروع ہوئی ہے اور رمل بھی ایک ہی مرتبہ ایسے طواف کے بعد مشروع ہوا ہے جس کے بعد سعی ہو۔
If he performed the sa'y between Safa and Marwah after Tawaf al-Qudum, he does not perform ramal in this tawaf, and there is no sa'y upon him. And if he did not perform the sa'y beforehand, he performs ramal in this tawaf and performs sa'y after it, because sa'y is only prescribed once, and ramal is only prescribed once in a tawaf after which sa'y is performed.
Translation: If the pilgrim has performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah after Tawaf al-Qudum, he will not perform ramal in this Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and sa'y is not required from him. And if he has not performed sa'y between Safa and Marwah beforehand, he will perform ramal in this tawaf and then sa'y after it, because sa'y is only prescribed once, and ramal is only prescribed once in a tawaf after which sa'y is performed.
Commentary: The issue is that if the pilgrim has performed sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum, he will not perform ramal in Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and sa'y is also not obligatory upon him. And if he did not perform sa'y earlier, he will perform ramal in this tawaf and then sa'y after it, because sa'y is only prescribed once, and ramal is also only prescribed once in a tawaf after which sa'y is performed.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the performance of ramal (quick walking with chest out) and sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah) in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling is conditional: if the pilgrim already performed sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum (the tawaf of arrival), then in Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he does not perform ramal, and sa'y is not required. If he did not perform sa'y earlier, then he must perform ramal in Tawaf al-Ziyarah and sa'y after it. The reasoning is that both sa'y and ramal are prescribed only once in Hajj. Ramal is specifically prescribed only in a tawaf that is followed by sa'y. Since Tawaf al-Qudum is the first tawaf and may be followed by sa'y, if sa'y was done then, Tawaf al-Ziyarah does not have ramal or sa'y. This is consistent with the Hanafi position that ramal is a sunnah in the first three rounds of the first tawaf that is followed by sa'y.

Key Terms
الرمل (ramal): Walking quickly with short steps and moving the shoulders, performed in the first three rounds of a tawaf that is followed by sa'y.
السعي (sa'y): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwah, a wajib act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Perform ramal and sa'y again
B) Perform ramal but not sa'y
C) Perform sa'y but not ramal
D) Neither ramal nor sa'y

Key Takeaway
Sa'y and ramal in Hajj are prescribed only once; Tawaf al-Ziyarah adds them only if sa'y was not performed earlier.

The Obligation of Two Rak'ahs After Every Tawaf
States the ruling of praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify the evidence (dalil) that establishes it as wajib.

Core Idea
Every tawaf, whether fard or nafl, must be concluded with two rak'ahs – this is a wajib act in the Hanafi school.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a key rite of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds this act to be wajib (necessary), based on the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this ruling helps you distinguish between fard and wajib in Hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states "he prays two rak'ahs after this tawaf." The Hanafi school classifies this as wajib, not fard. Why? Because the proof is from ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut), not from a definitive text.
In Hanafi usul, fard requires qat'i proof; wajib can be from zanni proof.
2
Locate the dalil
The author says "because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs." This is based on the Prophet's ﷺ practice of always praying two rak'ahs after tawaf.
The exact hadith is not quoted, but the principle is well established in Hanafi sources.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies to all tawafs, whether fard (like Tawaf al-Ziyarah) or nafl (supererogatory). The text explicitly says "whether the tawaf is fard or nafl."
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is consider these two rak'ahs as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib. The difference stems from the weight of the evidence.
The Hanafi school relies on the continuous practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
5
Apply the ruling
If a pilgrim omits these two rak'ahs, the tawaf remains valid, but he must make them up later (qada) because it is a wajib. Deliberate neglect incurs sin and may require dam.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ هَذَا الطَّوَافِ لِأَنَّ خَتَمَ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بِرَكْعَتَيْنِ فَرَضًا كَانَ الطَّوَافُ أُونَفَلًا لِمَا بَيَّنَا قَالَ وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ النِّسَاء لَكِنَّ بِالْحَلْقِ السَّابِقِ إِذْ هُوَ الْمُحَلَّلَ لَا بِالطَّوافِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ أَخَرَ عَمَلُهُ فِي حَقِّ النِّسَاءِ
ترجمہ اور اس طواف زیارت کے بعد دو رکعت نماز پڑھے کیونکہ طواف کا ختم دورکعت کے ساتھ ہے طواف فرض ہویا نفل ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور حاجی کے لئے عورتیں حلال ہو گئیں لیکن حلق سابق سے اس لئے کہ وہی محلل ہے نہ کہ طواف سے مگر یہ کہ اس کا عمل عورتوں کے حق میں مؤخر ہو گیا۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
And he prays two rak'ahs after this tawaf, because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is fard or nafl, due to what we have explained. He said: And women become permissible for him, but due to the previous shaving (halq), for it is the one that makes permissible, not the tawaf, except that its effect is delayed with regard to women.
Translation: And he should pray two rak'ahs after this tawaf, because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is obligatory or supererogatory, for the reason we have stated. And the pilgrim's women become permissible to him, but due to the prior shaving, for that is what makes permissible, not the tawaf, except that its effect is delayed regarding women.
Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The author states that after any tawaf—whether it is fard (like Tawaf al-Ziyarah) or nafl—two rak'ahs must be prayed. This is based on a general principle that every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs. Then the author clarifies that Tawaf al-Ziyarah itself does not make marital relations permissible; it is the shaving of the head (halq) that accomplishes tahallul (the state of being out of ihram). However, the effect of halq regarding women is delayed until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, meaning that even if one shaves before tawaf, marital relations are not permitted until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The commentary notes that this is clear.

Key Terms
الحلق (halq): Shaving the head, which is a rite of Hajj that initiates tahallul (release from ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah
B) It is wajib
C) It is optional
D) It is fard

Key Takeaway
Praying two rak'ahs after every tawaf, including Tawaf al-Ziyarah, is a wajib act in the Hanafi school; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the tawaf.

The Sequence of Tahallul: Halq and Tawaf
Clarifies the interaction between halq and tawaf for permissibility of marital relations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of marital relations after Hajj, identifying the role of halq (head shaving) and the deferred effect regarding women.

Core Idea
Halq causes partial tahallul, but full permissibility of marital relations requires completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

This lesson examines a subtle ruling in the Hajj rites: permissibility of marital relations. The passage clarifies that shaving the head (halq) is the primary cause of tahallul (release from ihram), not Tawaf al-Ziyarah. However, the effect of halq with respect to women is delayed until Tawaf is performed. Understanding this sequence is important for a correct understanding of Ihram restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on permissibility
The passage states 'women become permissible for him, but due to the previous shaving (halq).' This means halq is the act that makes marital relations permissible in principle.
2
Understand the role of halq
Halq (and similarly taqsir) is a wajib rite that initiates tahallul. Without halq, the pilgrim remains in ihram regardless of tawaf.
In Hanafi, halq is wajib; if omitted, the pilgrim stays in ihram and must compensate.
3
Note the delay in effect regarding women
The passage says 'except that its effect is delayed with regard to women.' This means that even if a pilgrim shaves before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, marital relations are not permitted until after the tawaf is performed.
The delay is specific to marriage; other ihram restrictions (like wearing sewn clothes) are lifted by halq.
4
Understand the reason for the delay
The Quranic verse (2:196) indicates that the Hajj is not complete until tawaf is performed, and the permissibility of marital relations is linked to completion.
Hanafi scholars derive this from the general principle of completion.
5
Apply the ruling
A pilgrim who shaves his head on the Day of Nahr but delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah must still avoid marital relations until after he performs that tawaf. If he engages in relations before tawaf, he has committed a sin and must offer a dam (sacrifice).
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

وَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَ هَذَا الطَّوَافِ لِأَنَّ خَتَمَ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بِرَكْعَتَيْنِ فَرَضًا كَانَ الطَّوَافُ أُونَفَلًا لِمَا بَيَّنَا قَالَ وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ النِّسَاء لَكِنَّ بِالْحَلْقِ السَّابِقِ إِذْ هُوَ الْمُحَلَّلَ لَا بِالطَّوافِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ أَخَرَ عَمَلُهُ فِي حَقِّ النِّسَاءِ
ترجمہ اور اس طواف زیارت کے بعد دو رکعت نماز پڑھے کیونکہ طواف کا ختم دورکعت کے ساتھ ہے طواف فرض ہویا نفل ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے اور حاجی کے لئے عورتیں حلال ہو گئیں لیکن حلق سابق سے اس لئے کہ وہی محلل ہے نہ کہ طواف سے مگر یہ کہ اس کا عمل عورتوں کے حق میں مؤخر ہو گیا۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
And he prays two rak'ahs after this tawaf, because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is fard or nafl, due to what we have explained. He said: And women become permissible for him, but due to the previous shaving (halq), for it is the one that makes permissible, not the tawaf, except that its effect is delayed with regard to women.
Translation: And he should pray two rak'ahs after this tawaf, because every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is obligatory or supererogatory, for the reason we have stated. And the pilgrim's women become permissible to him, but due to the prior shaving, for that is what makes permissible, not the tawaf, except that its effect is delayed regarding women.
Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on praying two rak'ahs after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The author states that after any tawaf—whether it is fard (like Tawaf al-Ziyarah) or nafl—two rak'ahs must be prayed. This is based on a general principle that every tawaf is concluded with two rak'ahs. Then the author clarifies that Tawaf al-Ziyarah itself does not make marital relations permissible; it is the shaving of the head (halq) that accomplishes tahallul (the state of being out of ihram). However, the effect of halq regarding women is delayed until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, meaning that even if one shaves before tawaf, marital relations are not permitted until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The commentary notes that this is clear.

Key Terms
الحلق (halq): Shaving the head, which is a rite of Hajj that initiates tahallul (release from ihram).
التحلل (tahallul): Release from the state of ihram; in Hajj, it occurs in stages: partial after halq and complete after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a pilgrim do to make marital relations permissible during Hajj?
A) Only shave his head
B) Only perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah
C) Both shave his head and perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah
D) Both sacrifice and shave his head

Key Takeaway
Halq causes partial tahallul, but marital relations are not permissible until Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed; violating this incurs sin and a required dam.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah: The Fard Tawaf of Hajj
Declares Tawaf al-Ziyarah as the fard tawaf with proof and timing details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, identify its Quranic proof, and explain the consequence of delaying it according to Abu Hanifah.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory pillar of Hajj; delaying it beyond the Days of Nahr incurs a dam.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, the author establishes Tawaf al-Ziyarah as the fard (obligatory) tawaf in Hajj, citing the Quranic command 'wa li-yattawwafu bi al-bayt al-'atiq'. He further clarifies its timing within the Days of Nahr and the penalty for delaying it. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the practical implications for a pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal classification. Is it fard, wajib, sunnah? The passage says 'this tawaf is the one made obligatory (fard) in Hajj, and it is a rukn (pillar).'
Note that fard and rukn are used interchangeably here; both indicate that omission invalidates Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited for the ruling. The author refers to the Quranic verse: 'and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29).
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form 'li-yattawwafu' indicates obligation (fard).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the verse proves the ruling. The command is general for all pilgrims, and the imperative implies a binding obligation.
The passage itself does not elaborate on the linguistic reasoning, but the Hanafi principle is that al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the timing and penalty for delay
Identify the time frame for performing this tawaf and the ruling if delayed. The text states it is timed with the Days of Nahr (10th–12th Dhul-Hijjah), and delaying beyond these days is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and requires a dam (sacrifice) according to Abu Hanifah.
The passage refers to a later chapter (jinayat) for details on the dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ هُوَ الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي الْحَجِّ وَهُوَ رُكُلٌّ فِيهِ إِذْ هُوَ الْمَامُورُ بِهِ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ وَيُسَمَّى طَوَافُ الْإِفَاضَةِ وَطَوَافُ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَيَكْرَهُ تَأخِيرُهُ عَنْ هذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا أَنَّهُ مُوَقَتْ بِهَا وَ إِنَّ أَخَرَهُ عَنْهَا لَرَمَهُ دَمَّ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَسَنتَيتُهُ فِى بَابِ الْحِسَايَاتِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ یہی طواف حج میں فرض کیا گیا ہے اور یہ اس میں رکن ہے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول وليطوفوا بالبيت العتیق میں اسی طواف کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور اسی طواف کا نام طواف افاضہ اور طواف یوم نحر ہے اور اس کو ان ایام سے مؤخر کرنا مکروہ ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ یہ طواف انہیں ایام کے ساتھ موقت ہے اور اگر حاجی نے طواف زیارت کو ان ایام سے مؤخر کیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر ایک دم لازم ہوگا اور ہم اس کو جنایات میں بیان کریں گے ان شاء اللہ تعالٰی ۔
تشریح طواف زیارت حج کے اندر فرض اور رکن کا درجہ رکھتا ہے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول وليطوفوا الآیہ میں اس کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔ اس کا دوسرا نام طواف افاضہ اور تیسرا نام طواف یوم نحر ہے۔ قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اس طواف زیارت کو ایام نحر سے مؤخر کرنا مکروہ تحریمی ہے۔ دلیل طواف قدوم کے ذیل میں گذر چکی کہ طواف زیارت ایام نحر کے ساتھ موقت ہے۔ لیکن مکروہ ہونے کے باوجود اگر طواف زیارت کو ان ایام سے مؤخر کر دیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر دم لازم ہو گا جس کی تفصیل کتاب الجنایات میں آئے گی۔
And he said: This tawaf is the one made obligatory in Hajj, and it is a rukn in it, because it is the one commanded in the saying of Allah Most High: 'and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House.' And it is called Tawaf al-Ifadah and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. And it is disliked to delay it beyond these days, for the reason we stated that it is timed with them. And if he delays it beyond them, then a dam is required according to Abu Hanifah, and we shall clarify it in the chapter of penalties, if Allah wills.
Translation: Al-Quduri said that this is the tawaf that is made fard in Hajj, and it is a rukn in it, because in the saying of Allah Most High 'and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' this tawaf is commanded. And it is named Tawaf al-Ifadah and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. And it is disliked to delay it beyond these days, for the reason we stated that this tawaf is timed with them. And if the pilgrim delays it beyond these days, then a dam is required according to Abu Hanifah, and we shall explain it in the book of penalties.
Commentary: Tawaf al-Ziyarah holds the rank of fard and rukn in Hajj, because Allah's command 'wa li-yattawwafu' is for it. Its second name is Tawaf al-Ifadah and third name is Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. Al-Quduri says that delaying this Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the Days of Nahr is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The proof passed under Tawaf al-Qudum that this tawaf is timed with the Days of Nahr. But despite it being disliked, if the pilgrim delays it beyond these days, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, a dam becomes necessary; its details will come in the book of penalties.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof stating that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory tawaf in Hajj (fard) and a rukn (pillar). The proof is the Quranic verse 'wa li-yattawwafu bi al-bayt al-'atiq' (and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House). This tawaf is also called Tawaf al-Ifadah and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. The author, al-Quduri, states that delaying it beyond the Days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul-Hijjah) is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because the tawaf is timed specifically with these days. If one delays it, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, a dam (sacrifice of a sheep) becomes obligatory. This is based on the principle that delaying a timed wajib act beyond its time without excuse incurs a penalty. The details are referred to later in the book of penalties (jinayat).

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is a rukn of Hajj; omission invalidates Hajj.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of Hajj, without which the Hajj is invalid.
دم (dam): A penalty of sacrificing a sheep for certain violations during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impermissible and Hajj becomes invalid
B) It is disliked but no penalty
C) It is disliked and a dam is required
D) It is permissible without any penalty

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory tawaf in Hajj; delaying it beyond the Days of Nahr is makruh and requires a dam.
