Timing of Rami on Yawm al-Nahr: Start and End Times
Determines start and end times for Rami on 10th Dhul Hijjah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the start and end times for Rami on Yawm al-Nahr and evaluate the evidence for the Shafi'i and intra-Hanafi disagreements.

Core Idea
Rami on Yawm al-Nahr begins at Fajr, not midnight — the hadith restricts it to the morning.

In this lesson, we examine a key timing dispute in Hajj: when exactly does Rami of Jamrat al-Aqaba begin on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah? The Hanafi school insists on waiting until Fajr, while Imam al-Shafi'i permits it after midnight. We also explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the end time. Understanding these proofs is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is Rami of Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr. The core dispute is about when its time begins and ends.
2
State the Hanafi position on start time
The Hanafi school holds that the time begins at Fajr (true dawn). This is based on a clear hadith.
The hadith 'لا ترموا جمرة العقبة حتى تصبحوا' explicitly restricts stoning until morning.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the Prophet's command: 'Do not stone Jamrat al-Aqaba until you enter the morning.' This establishes Fajr as the start.
A secondary narration mentions 'until the sun rises', which indicates virtue but not obligation.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i position and their dalil
Al-Shafi'i argues that Rami begins after midnight, citing the hadith that the Prophet permitted shepherds to stone at night.
The Hanafi response interprets that hadith as referring to the nights of the 11th and 12th, not the 10th.
5
Analyse the end time dispute
Abu Hanifa says the time extends to sunset, based on the hadith 'the first of our rituals on this day is Rami', making the entire day the time. Abu Yusuf restricts it to Zawal.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa, as the day ends at sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یوم انحر کور می کا وقت کب سے شروع ہوتا ہے
فَأَمَّا يَوْمُ التَّحْرِ فَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الرَّمَى فِيهِ مِنْ وَقْتِ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي أَوَّلُهُ بَعْدَ نِصْفِ اللَّيْلِ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَخَصّ لِلرِّعَاءِ أَنْ يَرْمُوا لَيْلًا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَرُمُوا حَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةَ إِلَّا مُصْبِحِيْنَ وَيُروى حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ فَيَتْبَتُ أصْلُ الوَقْتِ بِالْاَوَّلِ وَالأفَضلِيَّةُ بِالثَّانِي وَتَأْوِيلُ مَارَوَى اللَّيْلَةَ الثَّانِيَةَ وَالثَّالِثَةَ وَلانَّ لَيْلَةَ النَّحْرِ وَقَتَ الْوُقُوفِ وَالرَّمَى يَتَرَتَبُ عَلَيْهِ فَيَكُونَ وَفَتَهُ بَعْدَهُ ضَرُورَةً ثُمَّ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ يَمْتَدُّ هَذَا الْوَقْتُ إِلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ أَوَّلَ نُسُكِنَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ الرَّمَى جَعَلَ الْيَوْمَ وَقْتالَهُ وَذِهَا به بِغُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَمَتَدَّ إِلى وَقْتِ الزَّوَالِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَارَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ ار بایوم نحر تو اس میں رمی کا اول وقت طلوع فجر کے وقت سے ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اول وقت آدھی رات کے بعد سے ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چرواہوں کو رات میں رمی کرنے کی اجازت دی۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کرنا مگر صبح میں داخل ہو کر ۔ اور روایت کیا جاتا ہے یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے ۔ پس اصل وقت حدیث اول سے ثابت ہوگا اور افضلیت حدیث ثانی سے ثابت ہو گی۔ اور تاویل اس حدیث کی جس کو امام شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے دوم اور سوم رات مراد ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ دسویں کی رات تو وقوف عرفہ کا وقت ہے اور رمی وقوف عرفہ پر مرتب ہے اس لئے رمی کا وقت لازما وقوف کے بعد ہو گا۔ پھر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ وقت غروب آفتاب تک ممتد ہوگا کیونکہ حضور پیلے نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس دن میں ہمارا اول نسک رمی ہے پس رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے رمی کا وقت یوم قرار دیا ہے اور آفتاب ڈوبنے سے دن جاتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ یہ وقت زوال تک دراز ہوتا ہے اور ابو یوسف کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کا وقت طلوع فجر کے بعد سے شروع ہوتا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یوم نحر میں رمی کا اول وقت آدھی رات کے بعد شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چرواہوں کو رات میں رمی کرنے کی اجازت دی ہے۔ اگر طلوع فجر سے پہلے رمی کی اجازت نہ ہوتی تو ۔ حضور رات میں رمی کرنے کی اجازت کیوں دیتے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کرو مگر صبح میں داخل ہو کر ۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کا وقت صبح صادق یعنی طلوع فجر سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ایک
As for the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr), the first time for Rami on it is from the time of Fajr. Al-Shafi'i said: Its first time is after midnight, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the shepherds to stone at night. Our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not stone Jamrat al-Aqaba until you have entered the morning.' And it is narrated: 'until the sun rises.' So the original time is established by the first hadith, and the virtue by the second. And the interpretation of what he (al-Shafi'i) narrated refers to the second and third nights. And because the night of Nahr is the time for standing (wuquf) and Rami is subsequent to it, so its time must after it necessarily. Then according to Abu Hanifa, this time extends until sunset, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed, the first of our rituals on this day is Rami' – he made the day its time, and the day ends with sunset. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it extends until the time of Zawal, and the proof against him is what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing of Rami on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr). It covers both the start time and the end time. Regarding the start time, the Hanafi school holds that it begins at Fajr (true dawn), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it begins at midnight. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'Do not stone Jamrat al-Aqaba until you have entered the morning', which establishes Fajr as the start. The hadith about shepherds stoning at night is interpreted as referring to the nights of the 11th and 12th, not the 10th. Regarding the end time, Imam Abu Hanifa says it extends until sunset, using the hadith 'the first of our rituals on this day is Rami' to show the entire day is the time. Abu Yusuf holds it ends at Zawal, but the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
یوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The Day of Sacrifice, i.e., the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-ʿaqaba): The largest stone pillar at Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) At midnight
B) At Fajr (true dawn)
C) After sunrise
D) At Zawal (noon)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires Rami on Yawm al-Nahr to be performed after Fajr, not at midnight, based on the explicit hadith restricting it to the morning.

When Does Stoning on Yawm al-Nahr Begin?
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on stoning start time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the start time of stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr, cite the primary evidence, and rebut the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr begins at Fajr, not midnight, based on explicit hadith and logical sequence.

The timing of the first stoning on the Day of Sacrifice is a well-known point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafis and Shafi'is. In this lesson, we examine the evidence from both sides, focusing on the Hanafi reliance on the Prophet's explicit command and the logical link between the night's standing at Muzdalifah and the subsequent stoning. By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi school insists on Fajr as the earliest permissible time.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the exact ruling: the time for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr begins at Fajr (true dawn). Stoning before that is not valid according to the Hanafi school.
The Hanafi view is derived from the hadith of the Prophet.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their Proof
Know that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the time begins at midnight. His evidence is the hadith in which the Prophet allowed shepherds to stone at night.
This hadith is general but must be interpreted in context.
3
Follow the Hanafi Response to the Shafi'i Proof
The Hanafi response: the shepherds' hadith applies only to the nights of the 11th and 12th, not the night of the 10th. The night of the 10th is reserved for standing at Muzdalifah.
This interpretation resolves the apparent conflict between the two hadiths.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
The practical consequence: Hanafis do not permit stoning before Fajr on the 10th; Shafi'is permit it from midnight. This affects the validity of the stoning for those who perform it earlier.
The difference is significant for pilgrims' schedules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَأَمَّا يَوْمُ التَّحْرِ فَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الرَّمَى فِيهِ مِنْ وَقْتِ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي أَوَّلُهُ بَعْدَ نِصْفِ اللَّيْلِ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَخَصّ لِلرِّعَاءِ أَنْ يَرْمُوا لَيْلًا وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَرُمُوا حَمَرَةَ الْعَقَبَةَ إِلَّا مُصْبِحِيْنَ وَيُروى حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ فَيَتْبَتُ أصْلُ الوَقْتِ بِالْاَوَّلِ وَالأفَضلِيَّةُ بِالثَّانِي وَتَأْوِيلُ مَارَوَى اللَّيْلَةَ الثَّانِيَةَ وَالثَّالِثَةَ وَلانَّ لَيْلَةَ النَّحْرِ وَقَتَ الْوُقُوفِ وَالرَّمَى يَتَرَتَبُ عَلَيْهِ فَيَكُونَ وَفَتَهُ بَعْدَهُ ضَرُورَةً
As for the Day of Sacrifice, the first time for stoning therein is from the time of dawn. Al-Shafi'i said: Its first time is after midnight, because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ permitted the shepherds to stone at night. Our proof is his ﷺ saying: 'Do not stone Jamrat al-Aqabah until you enter the morning.' And it is narrated: 'until the sun rises.' Thus the original time is established by the first [hadith], and the virtue by the second. The interpretation of what he narrated [applies to] the second and third nights, and because the night of sacrifice is the time for standing [at Muzdalifah], and stoning is consequent upon it, so its time must necessarily be after it.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the start of the stoning time on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that the time begins at Fajr (true dawn). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it begins at midnight. The Shafi'i evidence is a hadith where the Prophet permitted shepherds to stone at night. The Hanafi response provides two pieces of evidence: first, the explicit command 'Do not stone until you enter the morning' (i.e., Fajr); second, a variant narration adds 'until the sun rises,' which indicates virtue, not obligation. The hadith cited by Shafi'i is interpreted as referring to the nights after the 11th and 12th, not the night of the 10th. Furthermore, logically, the night of the 10th is for standing at Muzdalifah (wujoof), and stoning is dependent on that standing, so it must occur after the night. Thus, the Hanafi view is that the valid time starts at Fajr, and the best time is after sunrise.

Key Terms
يَوْمُ التَّحْرِ (yawm al-nahr): The Day of Sacrifice, 10th Dhul Hijjah.
مُصْبِحِينَ (musbihin): Entering the morning; at Fajr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr begin?
A) At midnight
B) At Fajr (dawn)
C) At sunrise
D) At zawal (noon)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr be performed after Fajr, not before, based on an explicit prophetic command and the logical order of Hajj rituals.

End Time of Rami on Yawm al-Nahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the end time for stoning on Yawm al-Nahr and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Stoning on Yawm al-Nahr is valid until sunset according to Abu Hanifa, not just noon.

Stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr is a key Hajj ritual. This lesson examines a disagreement within the Hanafi school: does the time for this stoning end at noon (zawal) or continue until sunset? We will examine the textual evidence and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prescribed time
First, recognise that the ruling concerns the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). Both Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree that the time begins at Fajr, but differ on its end.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the time continues until sunset. His proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'Indeed, the first of our rituals in this day is stoning.' The word 'yawm' (day) linguistically lasts until sunset.
The hadith is a strong textual evidence.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf maintains that the time ends at zawal (noon). His basis is likely the Prophet's own practice of performing the stoning before noon, although the exact reasoning is not detailed here.
This is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Analyse the tarjih (preference)
The author (Al-Marghinani) states 'the proof against him is what we have narrated', indicating that Abu Hanifa's hadith is considered stronger. The explicit text overrides inference from practice.
Tarjih: Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is that stoning is valid until sunset, though performing it before noon is more virtuous. Stoning after sunset is valid but disliked.
This is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ يَمْتَدُّ هَذَا الْوَقْتُ إِلى غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ أَوَّلَ نُسُكِنَا فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ الرَّمَى جَعَلَ الْيَوْمَ وَقْتًا لَهُ وَيَذْهَبُ الْيَوْمُ بِغُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَمَتَدَّ إِلى وَقْتِ الزَّوَالِ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا رَوَيْنَا
Then, according to Abu Hanifa, this time extends until sunset, because of his ﷺ saying: 'Indeed, the first of our rituals in this day is stoning.' He made the day a time for it, and the day ends with sunset. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it extends until the time of zawal (noon). The proof against him is what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage deals with the end time for stoning on Yawm al-Nahr within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the time extends until sunset. His evidence is the Prophet's statement that stoning is the first ritual of the day, making the entire day (which ends at sunset) the time for stoning. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the time only extends until zawal (noon), based on the practice of the Prophet who performed the stoning before noon. However, the author affirms that Abu Hanifa's view is correct because the hadith uses 'yawm' (day), which linguistically lasts until sunset. The detailed ruling provided in the Urdu commentary further explains that stoning is permissible from Fajr to sunrise with dislike, from sunrise to zawal as the preferred time, from zawal to sunset with dislike, and after sunset until night with dislike. Thus, the general end time is sunset according to the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
زَوَال (zawal): The sun's declination from the meridian; noon.
غُرُوب (ghurub): Sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Until sunrise
B) Until zawal (noon)
C) Until sunset
D) Until midnight

Key Takeaway
The end time for stoning on Yawm al-Nahr is sunset according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Delaying the Stoning to Night or Next Day
Ruling on stoning after sunset or on following day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for delaying the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah to night or the next day and explain the requirement for a dam.

Core Idea
Stoning at night after sunset is valid without penalty; delaying to next day requires a dam.

Hajj rituals have precise times, but circumstances can cause delays. This lesson examines two scenarios: stoning after sunset on the day of sacrifice, and stoning on the following day. The ruling hinges on whether the delay exceeds the day itself. Understanding these nuances helps avoid unnecessary penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between delaying stoning to the night (after sunset but before dawn of the 11th) and delaying to the next day (the 11th of Dhul Hijjah).
Night here means the night following Yawm al-Nahr.
2
State the ruling for night delay
If the pilgrim stones after sunset but before the next dawn, the stoning is valid and no dam is required. This is based on the hadith of the shepherds who were permitted to stone at night.
3
State the ruling for next day delay
If the pilgrim delays stoning until the 11th (the first day of tashreeq), he must still stone because the 11th is also a time for stoning (jins al-ramy). However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a dam becomes wajib because the stoning was delayed from its specific time.
The dam is due for missing the optimal time, not for invalidity.
4
Identify the evidence
The night delay ruling is supported by the hadith: 'He permitted the shepherds to stone at night.' The next day delay ruling is based on the general principle that stoning on the days of tashreeq is valid, but Abu Hanifa adds the dam for delay.
The dam is from Abu Hanifa's madhhab; other imams may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اخر إلى اللّيل زماهُ ولاشى عليه لحديث الرعاء وإنْ أَخَرَهُ إِلَى الغدر ماه لأنه وقت جنسِ الرَّمَى وَعَلَيْهِ عَلَيْهِ لِحَدِيثِ ده عند أبي حَنِيفَةَ لتأخيره عن وقته كما هو مذهلة
And if he delays it to the night, he stoners and nothing is incumbent upon him, due to the hadith of the shepherds. And if he delays it to the next day, he stones because it is a time for the genus of stoning, and upon him [is a sacrifice] according to Abu Hanifa, because of delaying it from its time, as is his madhhab.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a pilgrim who delays the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr. If he delays until the night (i.e., after sunset but before dawn of the 11th), he can still stone at night and nothing additional is required (no dam). This is based on the hadith where the Prophet allowed shepherds to stone at night, indicating that stoning at night is permissible without penalty. If he delays until the next day (the 11th of Dhul Hijjah), he must still stone because the 11th is also a day for stoning in general (it is one of the days of tashreeq). However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory because he has delayed the stoning from its prescribed time (the 10th). The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa: delaying a Hajj ritual from its specific time requires a dam.

Key Terms
دَم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as compensation for delaying a wajib ritual.
جنس الرمي (jins al-ramy): The genus/category of stoning; refers to the days of tashreeq which are all valid times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must stone and also offer a sacrifice (dam)
D) He must repeat Hajj

Key Takeaway
Stoning at night after Yawm al-Nahr is valid without penalty; delaying to the next day requires a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Timing of Rami Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute and detailed timing ruling for rami on Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissible and recommended times for rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument.

Core Idea
Rami on Yawm al-Nahr is valid from dawn to sunset; sunrise to zawal is best, other times are permissible with karahah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a key disputed ruling in Hajj: the timing of rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr. The author reconciles contradictory hadiths, defends the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i school, and presents a detailed breakdown of times with varying levels of recommendation and dislike. Understanding this ruling is essential for pilgrims and muftis alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
Rami jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib act of Hajj. The dispute is about the time window in which it must be performed.
2
Understand the reconciliation of the two hadiths
One hadith implies rami can be done from dawn (except those who become morning), another indicates the best time is after sunrise. The author reconciles by making dawn the permissible start and sunrise the preferred start.
The first hadith is about the original time, the second about the preferred time.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i uses a hadith allowing shepherds to rami at night. The Hanafi response: that refers to nights of 11th and 12th, subordinate to preceding days. The night of Yawm al-Nahr is for Muzdalifah stay, not rami.
Nights are subordinate to preceding days, not following days.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds the time extends until sunset; Abu Yusuf holds it ends at zawal (midday). The author sides with Abu Hanifa based on a stronger hadith.
The hadith 'our first act on this day is rami' uses 'day' which applies until sunset.
5
Apply the detailed time breakdown
From dawn to sunrise: waqt jawaz with karahah. From sunrise to zawal: waqt sunnah. From zawal to sunset: waqt jawaz with karahah. From sunset to end of night: waqt jawaz with karahah (but still valid).
The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's: time until sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب النج
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
روایت میں ہے حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمس یعنی جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کرو۔ یہاں تک کہ آفتاب طلوع ہو جائے ۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ت کہ یوم نحر میں ہی کا وقت طلوع آفتاب کے بعد شروع ہوتا ہے۔ فاضل مصنف نے دونوں روایتوں میں تطبیق دیتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ حديث اول إِلَّا مُضبحِينَ سے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کا اصل وقت ثابت ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث حتى تطلع الشمس سے افضل وقت تَطْلُعَ کا ثبوت ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ طلوع فجر کے بعد یوم نحر میں جمر کے عقبہ کی رمی کرنا جائز ہے اور طلوع آفتاب کے بعد رمی کرنا افضل ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ روایت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں گیارہویں اور بارہویں کی رات مراد ہے مثلاً جب گیارہویں کو ری کا وقت شروع ہوا تو دن ختم ہو کر آخر رات تک رہتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ رمی کے حق میں راتیں سابقہ دنوں کے تابع ہوتی ہیں نہ کہ بعد میں نے والے دنوں کے۔ پس حضور بیت نے مندر کی وجہ سے چرواہوں کو اس بات کی رخصت دی کہ ۱۱ یا ۱۲ کے دن کی رمی کو رات میں ادا یں ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یوم نحر کی رات وقوف مزدلفہ کا وقت ہے اور رمی وقوف پر مرتب ہے اس لئے رمی کا وقت وقوف کے بعد ہو ۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ رمی کا وقت رات گذر کر صبح سے شروع ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام اعظم کے نزدیک یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کا وقت غروب آفتاب تک ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے اگه اس دن یعنی یوم نحر میں ہمارا پہلا عمل رمی کرنا ہے اس حدیث میں رسول خدا سے نے رمی کا وقت یوم قرار دیا ہے اور یوم کا اطلاق غروب تک ہوتا ہے اس لئے رمی کا وقت غروب تک ہوگا۔ لیکن یوم نحر میں وقت رمی کے سلسلہ میں تفصیل یہ ہے کہ یوم نحر کی طلوع فجر کے بعد ی، طلوع آفتاب تک مع الكراہت وقت جواز ہے اور طلوع آفتاب سے زوال تک وقت مسنون سے اور زوال کے بعد سے غروب تک بالا کراہت وقت جواز سے اور غروب کے بعد سے آخر رات تک مع الکراہت وقت جواز ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ یہ نجو میں رمی کا وقت زوال آفتاب تک رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ کے رسول نے نے زوال سے پہلے رمی فرمائی ہے لیکن ابو یوسف کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جس کو ہم سابق میں روایت کر چکے۔
The book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume three. There is a narration: 'until the sun rises' meaning do not throw jamrat al-Aqabah until the sun rises. From this hadith it is known that the time for Yawm al-Nahr begins after sunrise. The author, reconciling the two narrations, said that from the first hadith 'except those who become morning' the original time for rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah is established, and from the second hadith 'until the sun rises' the best time is established. The conclusion is that after dawn on Yawm al-Nahr, rami of jamrat al-Aqabah is permissible, and after sunrise it is better. The response to the narration presented by Imam al-Shafi'i is that in the hadith, the night of the 11th and 12th is meant; for example, when the time for rami on the 11th begins, it lasts from the end of the day until the end of the night. The conclusion is that with respect to rami, nights are subordinate to the preceding days, not to the following days. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave permission to the shepherds to perform the rami of the 11th or 12th at night due to the temple? The second proof is that the night of Yawm al-Nahr is the time for staying at Muzdalifah, and rami is dependent on staying, so the time of rami is after staying. Thus it is established that the time for rami begins after the night passes and at morning. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to Imam al-A'zam, the time for rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr extends until sunset, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'On this day, i.e., Yawm al-Nahr, our first act is rami.' In this hadith, the Messenger of Allah designated the time of rami as 'the day', and 'day' applies until sunset, so the time for rami is until sunset. But the detail regarding the time on Yawm al-Nahr is that after dawn until sunrise, with dislike, it is a time of permissibility; from sunrise to midday it is the recommended time; from midday until sunset, with dislike, it is a time of permissibility; and from sunset until the end of the night, with dislike, it is a time of permissibility. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that the time for rami on this day lasts until midday, because the Messenger of Allah performed rami before midday. But against Abu Yusuf, the hadith which we narrated earlier is evidence.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and detailed ruling on the timing of rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr. The author first presents two hadiths: one indicating that rami should be done after sunrise (the best time), and another indicating that it can be done from dawn (the original time). He reconciles them by stating that the original permissible time begins at dawn, but the preferred time is after sunrise. Then he addresses an objection from the Shafi'i school, which cites a hadith about allowing shepherds to rami at night; the Hanafi response is that the hadith refers to the nights of the 11th and 12th, which are subordinate to the preceding days, not the following day. Next, he states Abu Hanifa's position that the time for rami on Yawm al-Nahr lasts until sunset, based on the Prophet's words 'our first act is rami' where 'day' means the entire day until sunset. He then provides a detailed breakdown of the ruling: from dawn to sunrise it is permissible but makruh; from sunrise to zawal (midday) it is sunnah (recommended); from zawal to sunset it is permissible but makruh; from sunset to end of night it is permissible but makruh. Finally, he mentions Abu Yusuf's view that the time ends at zawal, but rejects it based on the stronger hadith. This is a classic Hanafi tafsil (detailed ruling) showing the gradation of times with respect to karahah and sunniyyah.

Key Terms
رمی جمرة العقبة (rami jamrat al-‘Aqabah): The stoning of the large pillar (jamrat al-‘Aqabah) on Yawm al-Nahr
یوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice
وقت جواز (waqt jawaz): A time when the act is permissible but not recommended; often with karahah

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to Abu Hanifa, what is the end time for rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr?
A) Sunrise
B) Zawal (midday)
C) Sunset
D) End of the night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits rami jamrat al-Aqabah from dawn to sunset on Yawm al-Nahr, with the best time between sunrise and zawal.

Ruling on Delaying Rami to Night or Next Day
Ruling on delaying rami with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the requirement of dam, and apply the principle that delaying a Hajj ritual from its specific time may require compensation.

Core Idea
Delaying rami to the next day triggers a dam according to Abu Hanifa; delaying to the same night does not.

In this lesson, we examine what happens if a pilgrim delays the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr. The Hanafi school distinguishes between delaying until night (same day) and delaying until the next day. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that delaying to the next day requires a sacrificial animal (dam), while his two students differ. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how the school balances textual permissions with the principle that each Hajj ritual has a specific time that must be observed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). It is wajib. The question is: what if it is delayed?
The ruling distinguishes two temporal thresholds: night of the same day and the next day (11th).
2
Analyze the first scenario: delay to night
If the pilgrim postpones rami until after sunset on the 10th, he should perform it at night. No dam (sacrifice) is required. The evidence is the hadith granting shepherds permission to stone at night.
The night is still part of Yawm al-Nahr in a broad sense; the hadith shows dispensation for pastoral necessity.
3
Analyze the second scenario: delay to next day
If the pilgrim does not stone even at night and delays until the 11th, he must still stone on the 11th. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a dam becomes wajib because the rami was delayed from its designated time (Yawm al-Nahr).
The 11th is a time for rami in general (jins al-rami), but the specific time for Jamrat al-Aqabah is the 10th.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa's position is that any deliberate delay from the specific time triggers dam. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani are reported to hold that no dam is required because the time for rami of all jamarat extends through the days of tashriq.
The source passage only mentions Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn's view is deduced from other Hanafi texts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that delaying to the next day does require a dam, following Abu Hanifa. The principle: delaying a wajib Hajj ritual from its specific time necessitates compensation unless a clear dispensation exists.
This reflects the school's general approach that time-bound rituals must be performed in their time to avoid penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یوم النحر کی رات کے وقت رمی کا حکم
وان اخر إلى اللّيل زماهُ ولاشى عليه لحديث الرعاء وإنْ أَخَرَهُ إِلَى الغدر ماه لأنه وقت جنسِ الرَّمَى وَعَلَيْهِ عَلَيْهِ لِحَدِيثِ ده عند أبي حَنِيفَةَ لتأخيره عن وقته كما هو مذهلة
ترجمہ اور اگر حاجی نے جمر کا عقبہ کی رمی گورات تک مؤخر کیا تو رات میں رہی کرلے اور اس پر کچھ لا زم نہیں ہے حدیث رعا ء کی وجہ سے اور اگر اس کو دوسرے دن تک مؤخر کیا تو رمی کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ وقت بھی جنس رمی کا ہے اور اس پر ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک قربانی لازم ہے کیونکہ رمی اپنے وقت سے مؤخر ہو گئی ہے جیسا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذ ہب ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ یوم نحر میں اگر جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی نہ کی۔ یہاں تک کہ رات آگئی تو رات میں رمی کرے اور اس پر دم وغیرہ کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں چرواہوں کو رات میں رمی کرنے کی رخصت دی گئی ہے اور اگر رات میں بھی رمی نہ کی۔ یہاں تک کہ گیارہویں تاریخ ہوگئی تو اس میں رمی کرے کیونکہ گیارہویں تاریخ بھی رمی کی جنس کا وقت ہے البتہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس پر دم واجب ہوگا کیونکہ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی اپنے وقت سے مؤخر ہوگئی اور امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے کہ نسک حج کا اپنے وقت سے مؤخر ہونا دم کو
Ruling on the time of night on Yawm al-Nahr. And if he delays it until night, he does it at night and nothing is incumbent upon him due to the hadith of the shepherds. But if he delays it until the next day, he does it because that time is also from the genus of rami, and upon him is a sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa because of delaying it from its time, as is his madhhab. Translation: If the pilgrim delayed the rami of jamrat al-Aqabah until night, he should do it at night and nothing is binding upon him due to the hadith of the shepherds. And if he delayed it until the next day, he should do it because that time is also from the genus of rami, and upon him, according to Abu Hanifa, one sacrifice is required because the rami was delayed from its time, as is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. Explanation: The issue is that if on Yawm al-Nahr he did not do rami until night came, he should do it at night and no dam or anything becomes obligatory upon him, the proof being the hadith in which shepherds were given permission to do rami at night. And if he did not do it even at night until the 11th day came, he should do it then because the 11th is also a time from the genus of rami. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a dam becomes obligatory because the rami of jamrat al-Aqabah was delayed from its time, and the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is that delaying a ritual of Hajj from its time necessitates a dam.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling on delaying rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr. It presents the ruling: if one delays the rami until night (i.e., after sunset on the 10th), he should perform it at night and no penalty (dam) is required, based on the hadith granting permission to shepherds to rami at night. If he delays it further until the next day (11th), he still performs it because the 11th is also a time for rami in general, but according to Abu Hanifa, a dam becomes obligatory because the rami was delayed from its specific time (Yawm al-Nahr). The commentary clarifies that the dam is wajib only in Abu Hanifa's view; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad may differ, though not explicitly stated here. The key principle is that delaying a Hajj ritual from its designated time requires compensation (dam).

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for a ritual mistake
رمی (rami): Stoning of the jamarat, a Hajj ritual
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The largest pillar representing the devil, stoned on Yawm al-Nahr

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Rami is invalid and must be repeated
B) Rami is valid with no penalty
C) Rami is valid but a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa
D) Rami must be done in Mina with an additional sacrifice

Key Takeaway
Delaying rami al-jamrat al-Aqabah to the next day requires a dam according to Abu Hanifa, while delaying to the same night does not.

Ruling on Performing Rami While Riding
Ruling on rami while riding with preference based on sequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing rami while riding and identify when walking or riding is preferred according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rami while riding is valid; walking is better when another rami follows, riding better when it does not.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from al-Quduri on the method of performing rami. The essential point is that riding does not invalidate the rami, but the preferred method depends on the sequence of jamarat on that day. This principle, attributed to Abu Yusuf, balances validity with the spiritual goal of humility during supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
What is the ruling on performing rami while riding? Is it valid or invalid? The passage states it is valid (ajza).
Validity is unconditional.
2
Understand the principle of preference
The passage introduces a conditional preference: if another rami follows, walking is better; if not, riding is better. This is based on the need for humility during the subsequent supplication.
The principle is from Abu Yusuf.
3
Apply to the days of Hajj
On Yawm al-Nahr, rami of Jamrat al-Aqabah is followed by no further rami, so riding is better. On the 11th and 12th, the first two jamarat are followed by another rami, so walking is better; the third jamrah is final, so riding is better.
This application follows logically from the principle.

قَالَ فَإِنْ رَمَاهَا رَاكِبًا أَجْزَاهُ لِحُصُولِ فَعَلِ الرَّمِ وَكُلُّ رَمَى بَعْدَهُ رَمَى فَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَرْمِيَهُ مَاشِيًّا وَإِلَّا غَيْرُ مِيهِ راكبا لِأَنَّ الْأَوَّلَ بَعْدَهُ وُقُوفٌ وَدُعَاءُ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَيَرْمِي مَاشِيًّا لِيَكُونَ اقْرَبَ إِلَى التَضَرُّعِ وَبَيَانُ الْأَفْضَلِ مَرْوى عَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ

Ruling on performing rami while riding. The book of Hajj. He (al-Quduri) said: If he does rami while riding, it suffices him because the act of rami is achieved. And every rami after which there is a rami, the better is that he does it walking, otherwise he does it riding, because after the first there is standing and supplication as we mentioned, so he does rami walking to be closer to humility. And the statement of the better is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Rami while riding is valid because the act of rami is achieved. Every rami after which there is another rami, it is better to do it walking; otherwise, riding is better, because after the first there is standing and supplication, so he does rami walking to be closer to humility. And the statement of preference is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Explanation: If someone does rami while riding, it is valid because the act of rami is achieved. Al-Quduri indicated a principle: if a rami is followed by another rami, then walking is better; otherwise, riding is better. According to this, on Yawm al-Nahr, rami of jamrat al-Aqabah is better riding because after it there is no rami. On the other days, for the first and second jamarat, since there is rami after them, he should do them walking; for the third jamrah, since there is no rami after it, he should do it riding. Sahib al-Hidayah gave the reason: if there is rami after, walking is better because after the first and second jamrah there is standing and supplication, so he does rami walking to be closer to humility. This statement of preference is narrated from Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri on performing rami while riding. It states that riding during rami is valid (ijza) because the essential act is achieved. It then lays out a principle: if a particular rami is followed by another rami on the same day (e.g., the first and second jamarat on the 11th and 12th), then it is better (afdal) to do it walking; if no rami follows (e.g., jamrat al-Aqabah on Yawm al-Nahr, or the third jamrah on other days), then riding is better. The reasoning is that after the first two jamarat, the pilgrim stands and makes supplication, and walking is more conducive to humility. This principle is attributed to Abu Yusuf. The commentary elaborates by applying the principle to the specific days. The ruling is straightforward: validity is not compromised by riding, but the recommended method depends on the sequence.

Key Terms
أجزاء (ajza'): The act is valid and fulfills the obligation
الأفضل (al-afdal): The better or more meritorious action, not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When no other rami follows after it
C) Always
D) When it rains

Key Takeaway
Rami while riding is always valid; the recommended method depends on whether another rami follows, as walking is better for humility before supplication.

The Hanafi Ruling on Staying Overnight in Mina
Ruling with proof on staying in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on staying overnight in Mina during rami nights and identify the evidence and reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Staying in Mina is sunnah, not wajib; leaving it causes no penalty.

This passage addresses a common question for pilgrims: must they stay overnight in Mina during the days of rami? The Hanafi school explains that while it is not obligatory, it is highly recommended. The ruling is based on the Prophet's practice and the actions of Umar, and the reasoning highlights its facilitative purpose. Let's examine the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is staying overnight in Mina during the nights of rami. The ruling is that it is sunnah; leaving it is makruh (disliked).
Makruh here means makruh tanzihi, which is closer to halal than haram.
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites the Prophet's (peace be upon him) practice of staying overnight and Umar's discipline for those who abandoned it.
Umar's discipline is considered a qawl sahabi, which is a source in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the reasoning
The purpose of the stay is to facilitate rami, not as a direct ritual act of Hajj. Therefore, it is not wajib.
If it were an act of Hajj itself, its omission would require a jabir.
4
Determine the consequence
Since it is sunnah, no compensatory act (dam or sadaqah) is required if omitted. The Hanafi position explicitly differs from Shafi'i.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: no penalty vs. dam required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منی میں رات گذار نے کا حکم
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ لَايَبِيتَ بِمِنَى لَيَالِيَ الرَّمَى لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بَاتِ بِهَا وعُمَر كَانَ يُؤَدِّبُ عَلَى تَرَكِ الْمَقَامِ بِهَا وَلَوْبَاتَ فِي غَيْرِهَا مَتَعَمِّدَ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَئْ عِندَنَا خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِي لأنَّهُ وَجَبَ لِيَسْهَلَ عَلَيْهِ الرَّمَى فِى أيَّامِهِ فَلَمْ يَكُن مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الْحَج فَتَرْكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الْجَابِرَ
ترجمہ اور رمی کی راتوں میں منی کے اندر رات نہ گزارنا مکروہ ہے اس لئے کہ حضور سی نے منی میں رات گزاری ہے اور حضرت عمر منی میں قیام ترک کرنے پر تادیب فرماتے تھے۔ اور اگر حاجی نے عدا منی کے علاوہ میں رات گزاری تو ہمارے نز دیک اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ قیام ثابت ہوا تا کہ حاجی پر رمی کے ایام میں رمی کرنا آسان ہو تو یہ فعل افعال حج نہ ہوا تو اس کے ترک سے نقصان پورا کرنے والا واجب نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ یہ بات مکروہ ہے کہ حاجی رمی کی راتوں میں منی میں رات نہ گزارے یعنی رمی کی راتوں میں منیٰ میں رات گزارنا ہمارے نزدیک سنت ہے اور امام شافعی وجوب کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے رمی کی راتوں میں منی
Ruling on staying overnight in Mina. It is disliked that he does not stay overnight in Mina during the nights of rami, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stayed overnight in it, and Umar used to discipline those who abandoned staying there. And if he stays overnight elsewhere intentionally, nothing becomes incumbent upon him according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because it (staying) was established to facilitate rami during its days, so it is not among the actions of Hajj, so abandoning it does not necessitate a compensatory act. Translation: It is disliked that the pilgrim does not spend the nights of rami in Mina, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) spent the night there, and Umar used to discipline those who abandoned staying. And if the pilgrim stays overnight elsewhere intentionally, nothing becomes wajib upon him according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because staying was established to make rami easy during its days, so it is not among the actions of Hajj, so abandoning it does not require a compensatory act. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that it is makruh for the pilgrim not to spend the nights of rami in Mina; i.e., spending nights in Mina during rami is sunnah according to us, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it to be wajib. The proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) spent the nights of rami in Mina.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the ruling on spending the nights of the rami days (11th, 12th, and optionally 13th) in Mina. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to not stay overnight in Mina, based on the Prophet's practice and Umar's discipline. However, if one intentionally stays elsewhere, no penalty (dam or any compensatory act) is required according to the Hanafi school, because staying in Mina is not a fundamental act of Hajj (manasik) but a facilitative act to make rami easier. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, considering it wajib and thus requiring a dam if omitted. The commentary clarifies that in the Hanafi school, it is sunnah, not wajib. The reasoning is that since it is not an act of Hajj in itself, abandoning it does not necessitate a jābir (compensatory act like dam).

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; leaving a sunnah is makruh tanzihi
الجابر (al-jabir): A compensatory act (like dam, sadaqah) that makes up for a deficiency in Hajj

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of intentionally not staying overnight in Mina during rami nights?
A) Dam required
B) Hajj invalid
C) Nothing wajib
D) Must repeat the night

Key Takeaway
Staying overnight in Mina during rami nights is a sunnah act; its omission is makruh but does not require any compensatory sacrifice.

The Inter-Madhhab Dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Overnight Stay in Mina
Inter-madhhab dispute on staying in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reason for the ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding staying in Mina, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Core Idea
For Hanafis, staying in Mina is sunnah; Shafi'is say wajib – the key is whether it is a ritual act or a facilitator.

One of the well-known differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools pertains to staying overnight in Mina during the rami days. While the Hanafis consider it a sunnah, Imam al-Shafi'i holds it wajib. The reasoning lies in how each school interprets the purpose of this practice. In this lesson, we break down both positions and their implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Staying in Mina is sunnah; leaving is makruh but no dam.
2
State the Shafi'i position
It is wajib; leaving requires a dam.
3
Present the Hanafi proof
Prophet's practice and Umar's discipline; the facilitative nature of the stay shows it is not an act of Hajj.
The purpose (ta'lil) is to ease rami, not a ritual.
4
Present the Shafi'i proof
Inferred from the Prophet's consistent practice and Umar's discipline – they argue it signals obligation.
Shafi'i usul: al-amr (command) and constant practice indicate wujub.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
Umar's discipline was for leaving a sunnah, not a wajib. The purpose is ease, not ritual. This leads to different compensation rules.
This is the tarjih: the Hanafi interpretation prevails in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منی میں رات گذار نے کا حکم
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ لَايَبِيتَ بِمِنَى لَيَالِيَ الرَّمَى لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بَاتِ بِهَا وعُمَر كَانَ يُؤَدِّبُ عَلَى تَرَكِ الْمَقَامِ بِهَا وَلَوْبَاتَ فِي غَيْرِهَا مَتَعَمِّدَ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَئْ عِندَنَا خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِي لأنَّهُ وَجَبَ لِيَسْهَلَ عَلَيْهِ الرَّمَى فِى أيَّامِهِ فَلَمْ يَكُن مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الْحَج فَتَرْكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الْجَابِرَ
ترجمہ اور رمی کی راتوں میں منی کے اندر رات نہ گزارنا مکروہ ہے اس لئے کہ حضور سی نے منی میں رات گزاری ہے اور حضرت عمر منی میں قیام ترک کرنے پر تادیب فرماتے تھے۔ اور اگر حاجی نے عدا منی کے علاوہ میں رات گزاری تو ہمارے نز دیک اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ قیام ثابت ہوا تا کہ حاجی پر رمی کے ایام میں رمی کرنا آسان ہو تو یہ فعل افعال حج نہ ہوا تو اس کے ترک سے نقصان پورا کرنے والا واجب نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ یہ بات مکروہ ہے کہ حاجی رمی کی راتوں میں منی میں رات نہ گزارے یعنی رمی کی راتوں میں منیٰ میں رات گزارنا ہمارے نزدیک سنت ہے اور امام شافعی وجوب کے قائل ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے رمی کی راتوں میں منی
Ruling on staying overnight in Mina. It is disliked that he does not stay overnight in Mina during the nights of rami, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) stayed overnight in it, and Umar used to discipline those who abandoned staying there. And if he stays overnight elsewhere intentionally, nothing becomes incumbent upon him according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because it (staying) was established to facilitate rami during its days, so it is not among the actions of Hajj, so abandoning it does not necessitate a compensatory act. Translation: It is disliked that the pilgrim does not spend the nights of rami in Mina, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) spent the night there, and Umar used to discipline those who abandoned staying. And if the pilgrim stays overnight elsewhere intentionally, nothing becomes wajib upon him according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because staying was established to make rami easy during its days, so it is not among the actions of Hajj, so abandoning it does not require a compensatory act. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that it is makruh for the pilgrim not to spend the nights of rami in Mina; i.e., spending nights in Mina during rami is sunnah according to us, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it to be wajib. The proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) spent the nights of rami in Mina.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the ruling on spending the nights of the rami days (11th, 12th, and optionally 13th) in Mina. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to not stay overnight in Mina, based on the Prophet's practice and Umar's discipline. However, if one intentionally stays elsewhere, no penalty (dam or any compensatory act) is required according to the Hanafi school, because staying in Mina is not a fundamental act of Hajj (manasik) but a facilitative act to make rami easier. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, considering it wajib and thus requiring a dam if omitted. The commentary clarifies that in the Hanafi school, it is sunnah, not wajib. The reasoning is that since it is not an act of Hajj in itself, abandoning it does not necessitate a jābir (compensatory act like dam).

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; leaving a sunnah is makruh tanzihi
الجابر (al-jabir): A compensatory act (like dam, sadaqah) that makes up for a deficiency in Hajj

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf between Hanafi and Shafi'i regarding staying in Mina?
A) Validity of Hajj
B) Necessity of dam
C) Number of nights required
D) Requirement of Ihram

Key Takeaway
The difference between sunnah and wajib in this case results in no vs. required compensatory sacrifice; the root lies in whether the stay is an act of Hajj itself or a means to facilitate rami.

Ruling on Stoning the Jamarat While Riding
States permissibility and best practice for stoning while riding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stoning the jamarat while riding and apply the preference rule based on whether a subsequent stoning follows.

Core Idea
Stoning while riding is valid; walking is preferred when supplication follows.

This passage from al-Quduri clarifies the permissibility of stoning the jamarat while riding. While the act is valid regardless, the Hanafi school distinguishes a preferred method based on whether the stoning will be followed by another. Understanding this contextual preference helps the pilgrim perform the ritual in the most meritorious manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its essential ruling
The passage states that if one stones while riding, it suffices. Identify that the core act (ramy) is achieved, confirming validity.
The ruling confirms that the mode of transport does not invalidate the stoning.
2
Recognize the contextual preference
The text divides stonings into two types: those after which another stoning follows, and those after which none follow. Note that for the first type, walking is afdal; for the second, riding is afdal.
The reason given: walking is closer to humility (tadarru') during the subsequent supplication.
3
Identify the evidence for the preference
The preference is attributed to Abu Yusuf, indicating it is a reliable transmitted ruling within the Hanafi school.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah, so it is authoritative.
4
Distinguish between validity and best practice
The ruling confirms validity (ajzā) regardless of mode. The preference (afdal) is a separate recommended practice, not a condition of validity.
Do not conflate the two: riding is permissible and valid; walking is better in specific contexts.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may require walking in all cases or consider riding makruh. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is based on their riwayah of the Prophet's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ رَمَاهَا رَاكِبًا أَجْزَاهُ لِحُصُولِ فِعْلِ الرَّمْيِ وَكُلُّ رَمْيٍ بَعْدَهُ رَمْيٌ فَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَرْمِيَهُ مَاشِيًّا وَإِلَّا غَيْرَهُ فَرَاكِبًا لِأَنَّ الْأَوَّلَ بَعْدَهُ وُقُوفٌ وَدُعَاءٌ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَيَرْمِي مَاشِيًّا لِيَكُونَ أَقْرَبَ إِلَى التَّضَرُّعِ وَبَيَانُ الْأَفْضَلِ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ
He said: If he stones them while riding, it suffices him because the action of stoning is achieved. And every stoning after which there is a stoning, then the best is that he stone it walking, and otherwise (if no subsequent stoning) then riding, because the first (stoning) after it is standing and supplication as we mentioned, so he stones walking to be closer to humility. And the statement of the best is transmitted from Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This is a ruling from al-Quduri on stoning the jamarat while riding. The ruling confirms that stoning while riding is valid and sufficient, as the essential act of throwing pebbles (ramy) is accomplished. The author then provides a general principle: for any stoning that will be followed by another stoning on the same or a later day, it is superior (afdal) to perform it on foot. Conversely, if no stoning follows (like the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice), then riding is better. The reason given is that after the first stoning, the pilgrim is required to stand and make supplication, and walking is more conducive to a state of humility and devotion. This preference is reported from Imam Abu Yusuf. Thus, in practice: on the days of Tashriq, the first and second jamarat are stoned on foot, while the third is stoned riding. This ruling is part of the established Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
رمی (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj.
ماشياً (māshiyan): Walking on foot.
تضرع (tadarru'): Humility and earnest supplication to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it better to stone the jamarat on foot?
A) When no subsequent stoning remains
B) When a subsequent stoning follows
C) Always
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Stoning the jamarat while riding is valid; the preferred method depends on whether a stoning with supplication follows.

Sending Luggage to Mecca During Hajj: A Makruh Act
Ruling on sending luggage to Mecca before completing stoning in Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending luggage to Mecca while staying in Mina as makruh tanzih and explain its two proofs: the practice of Caliph Umar and the principle of avoiding heart distraction.

Core Idea
Sending luggage to Mecca before finishing stoning distracts the heart, making it makruh tanzih.

This lesson addresses a specific Sunan of Hajj: the pilgrim's state of mind during the days of Tashriq. The Hanafi school considers it makruh to send one's belongings ahead to Mecca before completing the stoning, as it creates worldly worry that detracts from worship. We will examine the ruling, its evidence, and the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Locate the specific action: sending heavy baggage (thiqal) to Mecca while personally staying in Mina until stoning is completed.
The act is defined by the combination of sending luggage and remaining in Mina.
2
Classify the ruling level
Determine the hukm: it is makruh tanzih (disliked), not haram. Note that it is a mild dislike due to distraction.
Makruh tanzih means the act is better avoided but not sinful in a major sense.
3
Trace the narrative proof
Identify the hadith-like evidence: the practice of Caliph Umar, who forbade and disciplined for this action, indicating disapproval.
Umar's practice is considered a source of law in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the rational cause
Understand the ta'lil: the luggage causes shughl al-qalb (heart preoccupation), which distracts from worship. This is the underlying reason for the ruling.
The Hanafi school often combines textual and rational proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الرَّجُلُ ثِقَلَهُ إِلَى مَكَّةَ وَيُقِيمَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَصْنَعُ وَيُؤَدِّبُ عَلَيْهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ يُوجِبُ شُغُلَ قَلْبِهِ
He said: And it is disliked that a man sends his heavy luggage to Mecca and stays (in Mina) until he stones, because it is narrated that 'Umar used to forbid it and discipline for it, and because it causes preoccupation of his heart.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This is a ruling on sending one's belongings to Mecca before completing the stoning. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzihi to send one's heavy luggage (thiqal, meaning baggage) to Mecca while personally remaining in Mina until the stoning is completed. The reason is twofold: (1) the practice of Caliph Umar who would discipline those who did this, indicating it is disliked; (2) sending luggage ahead creates mental distraction (shughl al-qalb) because the person will be concerned about his belongings, detracting from the focus on worship. The lesson is that the pilgrim should keep his mind free from worldly concerns during the rituals.

Key Terms
ثقل (thiqal): Heavy baggage or belongings.
شغل قلب (shughl qalb): Preoccupation of the heart causing distraction from worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a waste of money.
B) It causes heart distraction (shughl al-qalb).
C) It contradicts a sunnah of the Prophet.
D) It is a form of riya' (showing off).

Key Takeaway
Sending luggage to Mecca while staying in Mina for stoning is makruh tanzih because it distracts the heart from worship.

The Sunnah of Stopping at al-Muhassab
Establishes stopping at al-Muhassab as a sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stopping at al-Muhassab and explain the evidence that makes it a sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intentional stop at al-Muhassab establishes it as a sunnah, not an obligation.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah act of Hajj: stopping at al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah) when returning from Mina to Mecca. The Hanafi school holds this to be a confirmed sunnah, based on the Prophet's deliberate action and his statement to the Companions. Understanding the reasoning and evidence helps distinguish confirmed sunnahs from mere customs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stopping at al-Muhassab when leaving Mina for Mecca. The ruling is sunnah (mustahabb), specifically a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
The text says 'فَصَارَ سُنَّةً' — thus it became a sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence is the Prophet's action (fi'l) and his statement: 'We will stop tomorrow at the Khayf of Banu Kinanah...' This is a sunnah ahad narration.
The hadith is cited in full in the source Arabic.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's stopping was intentional (qasdan), not coincidental. His statement indicates he planned the stop, and the reason given (to show Allah's victory) shows it was a desired act. Thus, it becomes a practice to emulate.
The phrase 'قَصْدًا' (intentionally) is key to establishing it as a sunnah.
4
Note the analogy (tashbih)
The text compares this sunnah to ramal (quick walking) in tawaf, which is also a confirmed sunnah. This reinforces that it is a desirable act, not an obligation.
The comparison 'كَالرَّمَلِ فِي الطَّوَافِ' shows it is similarly established.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf
The text indicates that the view of its being a sunnah is 'the correct view' (al-ashah), implying some scholars may not consider it sunnah. However, the Hanafi position is clear and relied upon.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih, but the mufta bihi is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ نَزَلَ بِالْمُحَصَّبِ وَهُوَ الْأَبْطَحُ وَهُوَ اسْمُ مَوْضِعٍ قَدْ نَزَلَ بِهِ رَسُولُ اللهِ ﷺ وَكَانَ نُزُولُهُ قَصْدًا هُوَ الْأَصَحُ حَتَّى يَكُونَ النُّزُولُ بِهِ سُنَّةً عَلَى مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَالَ لِأَصْحَابِهِ: إِنَّا نَازِلُونَ غَدًا عِنْدَ خَيْفِ بَنِي كِنَانَةَ حَيْثُ تَقَاسَمَ الْمُشْرِكُونَ فِيهِ عَلَى شِرْكِهِمْ يُشِيرُ إِلَى جَهْدِهِمْ عَلَى هِجْرَانِ بَنِي هَاشِمٍ فَعَرَفْنَا أَنَّهُ نَزَلَ بِهِ إِرَاءَةً لِلْمُشْرِكِينَ لَطِيفَ صُنْعِ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِهِ فَصَارَ سُنَّةً كَالرَّمَلِ فِي الطَّوَافِ
And when he leaves (from Mina) to Mecca, he should stop at al-Muhassab, which is al-Abtah, and it is the name of a place where the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stopped, and his stopping was intentional, that is the correct view, so that stopping there becomes a sunnah, as it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said to his companions: 'We will stop tomorrow at the Khayf of Banu Kinanah, where the polytheists took oaths in their polytheism.' He indicated their effort in boycotting Banu Hashim. So we knew that he stopped there to show the polytheists the delicate act of Allah Almighty with him. Thus it became a sunnah, like the raml in tawaf.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of stopping at al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah) when returning from Mina to Mecca after completing the stoning. The Hanafi position is that it is a sunnah muakkadah to spend some time there, following the Prophet's example. The text explains that the Prophet's stopping there was intentional (qasdan), not by chance, making it a sunnah. The hadith mentions Khayf Banu Kinanah, the place where the polytheists plotted against Banu Hashim. The Prophet stopped there to display Allah's victory over them. This act is likened to the raml (quick walking) in tawaf, which is also a sunnah. Practically, it is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
محصب (al-Muḥaṣṣab): A place between Mecca and Mina where the Prophet stopped.
ابطح (al-Abṭaḥ): Another name for al-Muhassab.
رمل (ramal): Quick walking with small steps during tawaf; a sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence that stopping at al-Muhassab is a sunnah?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran.
B) The Prophet intentionally stopped there and told his companions they would do so.
C) It is a historical custom from the pre-Islamic era.
D) The Companions unanimously agreed on its obligation.

Key Takeaway
Stopping at al-Muhassab is a sunnah muakkadah, proven by the Prophet's intentional act and statement.

Legal Status of Tawaf as-Sadr: Wajib in Hanafi School
Ruling + proof + inter-madhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf as-Sadr, explain the proof from hadith, and distinguish the practical consequence of the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Tawaf as-Sadr is wajib, not sunnah—the Prophet's command and the exemption for menstruating women prove its obligatory nature.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding Tawaf as-Sadr (farewell tawaf). The matn declares it wajib, and then provides the textual proof and a logical argument from the exemption granted to menstruating women. As a student of Hanafi fiqh, you must understand not only the ruling but also the istidlal (legal reasoning) that supports it, because it illustrates how a zanni dalil (a hadith ahad) can establish wujub in our school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi ruling
Read the matn: 'Wa huwa wajib 'indana' — Tawaf as-Sadr is wajib in our school. This is the core hukm.
Wajib is distinct from fard; omission requires a dam (sacrifice) but does not invalidate Hajj.
2
Locate the primary dalil (hadith)
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last covenant with the House be tawaf.' Identify the imperative 'فليكن' which, per Hanafi usul, indicates wujub.
Thubut is zanni (ahad hadith), so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Analyse the secondary proof (rukhsah for menstruating women)
The text mentions that the Prophet ﷺ granted a concession (rukhsah) to menstruating women, exempting them from this tawaf. This implies it is an act from which a valid excuse (hayd) exempts one—if it were merely sunnah, no exemption would be needed.
This is an argument from the absence of a qarinah (context) that could downgrade the imperative to nadb.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In Hanafi school, omitting Tawaf as-Sadr requires a sacrifice (dam); in Shafi'i school, no compensation is needed. This difference affects pilgrims who miss this tawaf.
This is the practical fruit of the dispute.
5
Identify the exceptions mentioned
The text exempts menstruating women (al-hayda) and the people of Makkah (ahl Makkah) because they do not depart (la yasdirun) and do not bid farewell.
This shows the ruling is not absolute; it applies to travellers leaving Makkah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ ثُمَّ دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ وَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لَا يَرْمُلُ فِيهَا وَهذَا طَوَافُ الصَّدْرِ وَيُسَمَّى طَوَافَ الْوَدَاع وَطَوَافُ أَخِرُ عَهْدِ بِالْبَيْتِ لِأَنَّهُ يُودِعُ الْبَيْتَ وَيَصَدِرُ بِهِ وَهُوَ وَاجِبْ عِندَنَا خِلَافَا لِلشَّافِعِيُّ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ حَجَّ هذا البَيْتَ فَلْيَكُنْ أخِرُ عَهده بالبيت الطَّواف وَرَحْصَ لِلنِّسَاءِ الحَيْضَ الأعلى أهل مَكَّةَ لأنّهم لا يَصْدِرُونَ وَلَا يُوَدِّعُونَ وَلَا رَمَلَ فِيهِ لِمَا بَيْنَا أَنَّهُ شُرِعَ مَرَّةَ وَاحِدَةً وَيُصَلَّى رَكَعَتَي الطَّوَافِ بَعْدَهُ لِمَا قَدِّمُنَا
He said: Then he enters Makkah and performs tawaf of the House for seven circuits, without ramal in them, and this is Tawaf as-Sadr, and it is called Tawaf al-Wida' and the last covenant with the House, because he bids farewell to the House and departs by it. It is wajib in our (view), contrary to al-Shafi'i, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever performs Hajj of this House, let his last covenant with the House be tawaf.' And he granted a concession to menstruating women, except for the people of Makkah, because they do not depart and do not bid farewell. And there is no ramal in it for what we have explained, that it is prescribed only once. And he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf after it for what we have presented.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal status of Tawaf as-Sadr (also called Tawaf al-Wida'). The Hanafi position, stated clearly in the matn, is that this tawaf is wajib (obligatory). The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Let his last covenant with the House be tawaf,' which indicates obligation (wujub) by the imperative form. The Shafi'i position considers it sunnah, not wajib. The Hanafi response includes the concession granted to menstruating women (who are exempted from this tawaf), which shows that it is not absolutely sunnah but rather wajib from which they are excused. The text also notes that ramal (quick pace) is not performed in this tawaf, as it is prescribed only once (in the first tawaf). After this tawaf, one prays two rak'ahs, as established previously.

Key Terms
طَوَافُ الصَّدْرِ (Tawaf as-Sadr): The farewell tawaf performed before departing Makkah after completing Hajj.
وَدَاع (wida'): Farewell; this tawaf is called Tawaf al-Wida' because it bids farewell to the Kaaba.
رَمَل (ramal): Quick pace with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf. Not performed in Tawaf as-Sadr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's evidence for considering Tawaf as-Sadr wajib?
A) It is included in the pillars of Hajj.
B) The Prophet ﷺ commanded it with an imperative and granted an exemption to menstruating women.
C) It is proven by consensus of all scholars.
D) It is analogous to Tawaf al-Qudum.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf as-Sadr is wajib in the Hanafi school; omission requires a dam (sacrifice), except for menstruating women and residents of Makkah.

Drinking Zamzam Water After Hajj: A Recommended Act
Commands drinking Zamzam water with prophetic precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (hukm) of drinking Zamzam water after Hajj and explain the proof that establishes it as mustahabb.

Core Idea
Drinking Zamzam water after Hajj is mustahabb, proven by the Prophet's own action.

This lesson addresses a specific recommended practice after completing Hajj: drinking from Zamzam well. The source passage provides both the instruction and the prophetic precedent. Understanding why it is mustahabb and not wajib is key to correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and determine what act is being prescribed and what category (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.) it falls under according to the Hanafi school.
The phrase 'يأتي زمزم ويشرب' indicates a recommended sequence, not a compulsory one.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) drawing water, drinking, and pouring the rest back.
The proof is a hadith ahad, which in Hanafi usul establishes a ruling at the level of zann.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Apply the Hanafi principle that the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates istihbab (recommendation) unless there is a contextual indicator of wujub (obligation). Here, there is no such indicator.
If the Prophet's action were obligatory, it would be designated as such by words or strong contextual clues.

Source Text

This is based on the prophetic practice: the Prophet ﷺ drew a bucket of Zamzam water himself, drank from it, and then poured the remaining water back into the well. This establishes the recommendation (istihbab) of drinking Zamzam water during Hajj. The act is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms

Recommended Actions at the Multazam and Leaving the Kaaba
Recommends kissing threshold and clinging to Multazam with manner of leaving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) actions at the Multazam and leaving the Kaaba, and distinguish them from obligatory acts.

Core Idea
Kissing the threshold, clinging to the Multazam, and leaving backwards weeping are mustahabb, not wajib.

After completing tawaf al-sadr, the pilgrim engages in acts of devotion and adab (etiquette) before leaving the Kaaba. This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines three specific recommended actions based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding their legal level (mustahabb) is crucial to avoid treating them as obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions
List the three actions described: kissing the threshold, clinging to the Multazam, and departing backwards weeping.
The Multazam is between the Black Stone and the door.
2
Determine the legal ruling
Note the word 'yastahibbu' (it is recommended). This indicates mustahabb, not fard or wajib.
Mustahabb means recommended; omission is not sinful and requires no compensation.
3
Examine the proof
The text cites a narration (riwaya) that the Prophet did this at the Multazam. This is a sunnah ahad, giving zanni thubut and zanni dalala, making it mustahabb.
The proof is the Prophet's action (fi'l), which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation unless it indicates obligation.
4
Apply the etiquette of leaving
The backward exit, weeping, and showing distress symbolize the pilgrim's reluctance to leave the sacred House. This is an expression of adab.
This is spiritual guidance, not a legal requirement.
5
Contextualize within Hajj completion
The passage concludes 'this is the explanation of the completeness of Hajj.' These acts complete the spiritual experience, not the legal validity.
Hajj is valid without these acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَحِبُّ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ الْبَابَ وَيُقَبِّلَ الْعَتَبَةَ وَيَأْتِيَ الْمُلْتَزَمَ وَهُوَ مَا بَيْنَ الْحَجَرِ إِلَى الْبَابِ فَيَضَعَ صَدْرَهُ وَوَجْهَهُ عَلَيْهِ وَيَتَشَبَّثَ بِالْأَسْتَارِ سَاعَةً ثُمَّ يَعُودَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ هَكَذَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَعَلَ بِالْمُلْتَزَمِ قَالُوا وَيُسْتَحَبُّ أَنْ يَنْصَرِفَ وَهُوَ يَمْشِي وَرَاءَهُ وَوَجْهُهُ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ مُتَبَاكِيًا مُتَحَسِّرًا عَلَى فِرَاقِ الْبَيْتِ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ فَهَذَا بَيَانُ تَمَامِ الْحَجِّ
And it is recommended that he comes to the door and kisses the threshold, and comes to the Multazam, which is the area between the Black Stone and the door, and places his chest and face on it, and clings to the curtains for a while. Then he returns to his family. Thus it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did at the Multazam. They said: And it is recommended that he departs, walking backwards with his face towards the House, weeping, distressed at the separation from the House, until he exits the mosque. This is the explanation of the completeness of Hajj.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage details the recommended (mustahabb) acts after completing tawaf al-sadr. The pilgrim should: (1) approach the door of the Kaaba and kiss its threshold; (2) go to the Multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door), press his chest and face against it, and cling to the curtain (kiswah) for a while. This is based on the Prophet's ﷺ practice. After these, (3) he should leave the Masjid al-Haram while walking backwards (facing the Kaaba), weeping and showing grief at parting from the House, until he exits. This concludes the rituals of Hajj. These acts are all mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The weeping and backward exit emphasize the adab (etiquette) of leaving the sacred place.

Key Terms
ملتزم (multazam): The area between the Black Stone (Hajar Aswad) and the door of the Kaaba, where it is recommended to cling to the wall while supplicating.
عتبة (atabah): The threshold of the door of the Kaaba, which is kissed as a sign of respect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Kissing the threshold, clinging to the Multazam, and leaving backwards weeping are mustahabb acts that complete the adab of Hajj but do not affect its validity.
