Farewell Tawaf is Wajib for Non-Makkans
Establishes wajib of farewell tawaf via hadith and exemption for Makkans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on farewell tawaf, identify the primary dalil (hadith), and explain why the command (amr) indicates wujub.

Core Idea
Farewell tawaf is wajib for non-Makkans, proven by an imperative without a counter-indication.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author establishes the obligatory nature of tawaf as-sadr (farewell tawaf) for pilgrims who are not residents of Makkah. The proof is a hadith commanding that the last act at the House be tawaf, interpreted through Hanafi usul as indicating obligation. A concession for menstruating women confirms that the obligation applies to those without excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is its hukm level? The act is tawaf as-sadr, and the ruling is wajib for non-Makkans.
The hukm is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is zanni al-thubut.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'Whoever performs Hajj of the House, let his last act be tawaf of the House.' Identify this as the primary textual evidence.
This hadith is a Sunnah ahad; its transmission is zanni.
3
Apply Hanafi usul to the dalil
The word 'fal-yakun' is an imperative (amr). In Hanafi usul, an amr indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah (contextual indicator) to the contrary. No such qarinah is present here.
The Shafi'i school also accepts amr for wujub, but they may find a qarinah in the concession.
4
Analyze the secondary proof
The concession for menstruating women to leave without farewell tawaf proves that the tawaf is obligatory for those not excused. If it were merely sunnah, there would be no need for a special concession.
This is a dalil al-khitab argument: the exception proves the rule.
5
Note the exception for Makkans
Sahib Quduri clarifies that Makkans are not required to perform farewell tawaf because they are not departing from a journey and do not bid farewell to the House.
The exemption is based on the absence of the reason for farewell tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے کہ جس نے بیت اللہ کا حج کیا تو اس کا آخری عمل بیت اللہ کا طواف ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور حیض والی عورتوں کو رخصت دی یعنی حیض و نفاس والی عورتوں کے لئے بغیر طواف صدر کے روانہ ہونا جائز ہے اس حدیث میں فلیکن امر ہے اور بلا قرینہ صارفہ امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اس لئے ثابت ہوگا کہ سیہ [؟] طواف واجب ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حائضہ عورتوں کو اس کی اجازت دی ہے کہ وہ بغیر طواف صدر کئے روانہ ہو جائیں۔ یہ بھی وجوب کی دلیل ہے ورنہ رخصت کی تخصیص کا کیا فائدہ ہوتا ۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ مکہ والوں پر طواف صدر واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ باشندگان مکہ نہ کہیں کے لیئے روانہ ہوتے ہیں اور نہ ہی بیت اللہ کو وداع کرتے ہیں۔ اس طواف میں رمل اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ رمل فقط ایک بار مشروع ہے اور وہ طواف قدوم یا طواف زیارت میں کیا جا چکا اس لئے اب دوبارہ کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے البتہ طواف صدر کے بعد طواف کی دورکعت پڑھ لے کیونکہ اول باب میں گذر چکا کہ ہر طواف دو رکعت کے ساتھ پورا ہو گا طواف خواہ فرض ہو یا غیر فرض ۔
Our proof is this hadith: whoever performs Hajj of the House of Allah, his final act should be tawaf of the House of Allah. And menstruating women were given a concession, meaning it is permissible for menstruating and postpartum women to depart without tawaf as-sadr. In this hadith, the word 'fal-yakun' is a command (amr), and without a diverting indicator, a command indicates obligation. So it is established that this tawaf is wajib. The second proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) permitted menstruating women to depart without performing tawaf as-sadr. This also proves obligation; otherwise what benefit would there be in specifying the concession? Sahib Quduri says: Tawaf as-sadr is not wajib on the people of Makkah because they are not departing from anywhere, nor do they bid farewell to the House of Allah. There is no raml in this tawaf because raml is legislated only once, and it has already been performed in tawaf al-qudum or tawaf az-ziyarah, so there is no need to repeat it. However, after tawaf as-sadr, one should pray two rak'ahs because it has passed in the first chapter that every tawaf is completed with two rak'ahs, whether the tawaf is fard or non-fard.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) concerning the Farewell Tawaf (tawaf as-sadr). It establishes that tawaf as-sadr is wajib for pilgrims who are not residents of Makkah. The author presents two proofs. First, a hadith that the last act at the House should be tawaf, phrased as a command ('fal-yakun'), which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation unless there is a counter-indication. The concession for menstruating women to leave without this tawaf confirms that it is otherwise obligatory. Second, the very existence of this concession implies that the tawaf is wajib for those without excuse. Sahib Quduri then clarifies that Makkans are not required to perform tawaf as-sadr because they are not leaving their home. Additionally, raml (quick walking with shoulders bared) is not done in this tawaf because it is a multi-day rite, only prescribed once. However, the two rak'ahs after tawaf are still performed as every tawaf requires them.

Key Terms
طواف صدر (tawaf as-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing all rites of Hajj before leaving Makkah.
امر (amr): A command form in Arabic that indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with shoulders bared during tawaf; not performed in farewell tawaf because it is a single rite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tawaf as-sadr not wajib on the people of Makkah?
A) Because they are already purified.
B) Because they are not departing from elsewhere and do not bid farewell.
C) Because they are exempt due to the concession for menstruation.
D) Because tawaf as-sadr is only performed once in a lifetime.

Key Takeaway
Farewell tawaf is wajib for non-Makkans, established by the command 'fal-yakun' without a counter-indication.

Drinking Zamzam Water: A Recommended Act
Ruling statement with prophetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on drinking Zamzam water during Hajj and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Drinking Zamzam water is mustahabb – a reward without sin for omission.

The pilgrim is encouraged to go to the well of Zamzam and drink from its water. This recommendation is rooted in the Prophet's own action, which serves as a model for believers. Understanding the category of 'mustahabb' helps distinguish between required and optional acts in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the text and determine what action is being described and its legal classification. The text says 'he goes to Zamzam and drinks from its water' – this is a recommended act (mustahabb).
The ruling is not fard or wajib, as there is no command or consequence for leaving it.
2
Locate the evidence
The text cites a narration: the Prophet himself drew water, drank, and poured the remainder back. This serves as the proof (dalil) for the recommendation.
The dalil is a single narration (Sunnah ahad), which in Hanafi usul can establish a sunnah or mustahabb but not an obligation.
3
Understand the legal category
In Hanafi fiqh, mustahabb (also called mandub or nafl) is an act that is rewarded when done but not sinful when omitted. It is distinct from sunnah (more emphasized) and fard/wajib (obligatory).
The Prophet's action here is interpreted as showing permissibility and desirability, not obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The evidence is an action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who personally drew water and drank. This establishes it as a sunnah act. The author does not discuss any obligation or compensation, indicating it is merely recommended.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, leaving it is not sinful.
زمزم (Zamzam): The well in Masjid al-Haram in Makkah.

Farewell Actions at the Kaaba: Kissing the Threshold and the Multazam
Lists recommended farewell acts with prophetic precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions at the Kaaba during farewell and identify their basis in the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Kissing the threshold and clinging to the multazam are sunnah acts that complete the farewell of Hajj.

This passage describes the final recommended acts at the Kaaba after completing Hajj. These acts, based on the Prophet's practice, are considered mustahabb and include physical expressions of love and regret at parting. The text also instructs on the proper manner of departure from the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
Read the text and list the actions described: going to the door, kissing the threshold, going to the multazam, placing chest and face, clinging to the curtains, and departing backwards.
2
Locate the multazam
The multazam is defined as the area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba. Understand its significance as a place for supplication.
Some texts call it 'multazam' or 'multaram'.
3
Note the prescribed manner of departure
The pilgrim should leave walking backwards, facing the Kaaba, weeping and sorrowful, until exiting the mosque.
This reflects the emotional attachment to the sacred house.
4
Recognize the proof
The text states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did this at the multazam, establishing it as a sunnah.
The proof is a direct prophetic action (fi'l).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (ruling_statement) detailing mustahabb actions at the end of Hajj. It recommends approaching the door of the Kaaba, kissing its threshold (the wooden barrier at the entrance), then going to the multazam (the area between the Black Stone and the door) and pressing his chest and face against it, clinging to the curtain for a while. This is based on the Prophet's action. After that, he should depart walking backwards, facing the Kaaba, weeping with regret at leaving the House, until he exits the mosque. This completes the description of the Hajj rituals. The phrase 'thus it is narrated' indicates the proof.

Key Terms
ملتزم (multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba, where it is recommended to cling.
عاتبة (atabah): The threshold of the Kaaba door.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the multazam?
A) The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba.
B) The door of the Kaaba.
C) The threshold of the Kaaba.
D) The area around the Kaaba.

Key Takeaway
Kissing the threshold and clinging to the multazam are sunnah acts rooted in the Prophet's example, expressing love and regret at leaving the Sacred House.

Tawaf al-Qudum Dropped When Entering Arafat First
Ruling on dropping tawaf al-qudum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tawaf al-qudum when entering Arafat directly and explain why no compensatory act is required.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah; omitting it due to change of order requires no compensation.

This passage addresses a practical Hajj scenario: if a pilgrim in ihram goes straight to Arafat without first entering Makkah, the tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) is dropped. The text explains the reasoning and emphasizes that since this tawaf is a sunnah (not wajib), no penalty like dam or sadaqah is owed. This distinction between sunnah and wajib is a key Hanafi principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and scenario
The act under discussion is tawaf al-qudum. The scenario: the muhrim does not enter Makkah but proceeds directly to Arafat and performs wuquf (standing).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling is that tawaf al-qudum drops (saqata) from him entirely. It is not required, nor can it be made up later in the same manner.
3
Analyze the proof (talil)
The text gives a reason: tawaf al-qudum is legislated at the beginning of Hajj such that the other actions follow in order. If that order is not observed, performing it later would not be considered sunnah.
The proof is not a specific text but a hikmah (wisdom) behind the legislation.
4
Determine the consequence
Nothing is due (la shay'a alayhi) because leaving a sunnah does not require a jabir (compensatory act). If it were wajib, a jabir (like dam) would be necessary.
Jabir refers to any compensatory act that makes up for a missed wajib.
5
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that sunnah omissions generally incur no penalty, even if the sunnah is muakkadah. The key is whether the act is wajib or sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِن لَم يَدْخُلِ الْمُحْرِمُ مَكَّةَ وَ تَوَجَّهَ إِلى عَرَفَاتٍ وَوَقَفَ فِيهَا عَلَى مَابَيَّنَا سَقَطَ عَنْهُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْحَجّ عَلَى وَجْهٍ يَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَيْهِ سَائِرُ الْأَفْعَالِ فَلَا يَكُونُ الْإِنْيَانُ بِهِ عَلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ الْوَجْهِ سُنَّةً وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ بِتَرْكِهِ لِأَنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ وَتَرْكُ السُّنَّةِ لَا يَجِبُ الْجَابِرُ
And if the muhrim does not enter Makkah and goes directly to Arafat and stands there in the manner we have explained, then tawaf al-qudum drops from him, because it is legislated at the beginning of Hajj in a way that the other actions follow it. So performing it in a different manner is not sunnah, and nothing is due on him for leaving it, because it is a sunnah, and leaving a sunnah does not require a compensatory act (jabir).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof). It addresses a scenario: if a person enters ihram but does not first enter Makkah, instead proceeding directly to Arafat and performs the standing at Arafat properly, then tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) is no longer required. The reason (talil) is that tawaf al-qudum is legislated such that the subsequent Hajj acts are arranged after it; if the pilgrim misses that order, the tawaf is not even sunnah to perform later. Since it is a sunnah (not wajib), leaving it incurs no penalty (no dam, etc.). The phrase 'jabir' refers to a compensatory act like dam or sadaqah that would be required for leaving a wajib.

Key Terms
طواف قدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon entering Makkah at the start of Hajj.
جابر (jabir): A compensatory act (such as dam) required for leaving a wajib; not required for leaving a sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return to Makkah for tawaf al-qudum.
B) Tawaf al-qudum drops and he owes a dam.
C) Tawaf al-qudum drops and nothing is due.
D) He should perform tawaf al-qudum after Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah of Hajj that is dropped if the pilgrim goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah, and no compensation is required.

Timing of Wuquf at Arafah: Hanafi vs Maliki
Defines the time for wuquf at Arafat and refutes Imam Malik's differing opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the beginning time of wuquf at Arafah, identify the textual evidence, and explain why the Maliki view is considered refuted.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Arafah must begin after noon; the Prophet's practice and hadith establish this, overruling Imam Malik's earlier timing.

The timing of wuquf at Arafah is a critical element of Hajj. The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's own action and a key hadith, holds that the valid period begins after the sun passes its zenith (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. Imam Malik differed, placing the start earlier. This lesson examines the proof and the refutation of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The beginning time for wuquf is after the sun's noon decline (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The ending time is dawn (fajr) of the 10th.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Two proofs are cited: (1) The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wuquf after noon. (2) The hadith 'Whoever catches Arafah by night has caught Hajj' indicates the time extends from the end of daytime through the night.
3
Understand the Maliki position
Imam Malik holds that wuquf begins either after dawn of the 9th or after sunrise, based on his own reasoning or a different narration.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi refutation
The text states that Malik's view is 'mahjuj' (refuted) by the transmitted evidence (narrations) that the Hanafis have provided. The Prophet's action and the hadith override any contrary opinion.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under the Hanafi ruling, wuquf before noon is not valid; one must be present after zawal. Under the Maliki view, wuquf from dawn or sunrise is valid. This difference affects pilgrims who stand before noon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِعَرَفَةَ مَا بَيْنَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ يَوْمِهَا إِلى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِنْ يَوْمِ التَّحْرِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الحجَّ فَأَوَّلُ وَقْتِ الْوُقُوفِ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ عِنْدَنَا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَقَفَ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ وَهَذَا بَيَانُ أَوَّلِ الْوَقْتِ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَةَ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَمَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَةَ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَهَذَا بَيَانُ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ وَمَالِكُ إِنْ كَانَ يَقُولُ إِنَّ أَوَّلَ وَقْتِهِ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ أَوْ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ فَهُوَ مَحْجُوجٌ عَلَيْهِ بِمَا رَوَيْنَا
And whoever catches the standing at Arafah between the noon decline of the sun on its day and the dawn of the day of sacrifice has caught Hajj. So the beginning time of standing in our view is after noon, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood after noon, and this is the explanation of the beginning time. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever catches Arafah by night has caught Hajj, and whoever misses Arafah by night has missed Hajj.' So this is the explanation of the ending time. As for Malik, if he says that its beginning time is after dawn or after sunrise, he is refuted by what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute (inter_madhhab_dispute) concerning the time for wuquf at Arafah. The Hanafi position is that the valid period for wuquf begins after noon (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and extends until the dawn (fajr) of the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr). The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wuquf after noon, and the hadith states that catching Arafah by night (i.e., during the night until dawn) counts as catching Hajj. Imam Malik holds that the time begins either after dawn of the 9th or after sunrise, which contravenes these narrations. The text refutes Malik by stating that his view is overruled by the transmitted proof (ma rawayna). The word 'mahjuj' means his argument is invalidated by the evidence we have reported.

Key Terms
زوال شمس (zawal al-shams): The moment the sun passes its zenith (noon).
محجوج عليه (mahjuj 'alayh): His argument is refuted or overruled by evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the valid time for wuquf at Arafah begin?
A) At sunrise on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
B) After the noon decline (zawal) on the 9th.
C) At sunset on the 9th.
D) At dawn on the 10th.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes that wuquf at Arafah must begin after noon, based on the Prophet's practice and the hadith, and considers the Maliki view refuted by this evidence.

When Tawaf al-Qudoom Is Dropped for Direct Arafat Travel
Statement of ruling on Tawaf al-Qudoom when Muhrim skips Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudoom when a Muhrim proceeds directly to Arafat and explain why no compensation is required.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudoom is Sunnah; omitting it by going directly to Arafat requires no compensation.

Many pilgrims wonder what happens to the arrival circumambulation (Tawaf al-Qudoom) if they head straight to Arafat without entering Makkah. This concise passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that the Tawaf is dropped and no penalty is incurred because it is a Sunnah, not an obligation. Understanding this ruling removes unnecessary worry and highlights the Hanafi classification of Hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Understand the exact condition: the Muhrim does not enter Makkah and goes directly to Arafat to perform Wuquf.
The key condition is not entering Makkah at all before Arafat.
2
State the Ruling
The text says Tawaf al-Qudoom is dropped (saqata) from such a Muhrim.
This is a clear statement of the ruling.
3
Analyze the Reason
The passage explains why: Tawaf al-Qudoom was prescribed at the beginning of Hajj so that the other acts (sa'i, wuquf, etc.) follow in order. Performing it later would not fulfill that order.
The wisdom (hikmah) is maintaining the sequence of rituals.
4
Classify the Hukm Level
The text explicitly calls it a Sunnah. In Hanafi fiqh, Sunnah is distinct from Fard and Wajib; its omission does not require compensation (jabir).
Contrast with Shafi'i school which may consider it Wajib.
5
Conclude on Consequence
Omitting Tawaf al-Qudoom in this scenario entails no dam or other jabir. The pilgrim's Hajj remains valid.
The passage ends with 'la yajib al-jabir' (compensation is not required).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ وَإِن لَم يَدْخُلِ الْمُحْرِمُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ وَوَقَفَ فِيهَا عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّا سَقَطَ عَنْهُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْحَجِّ عَلَى وَجْهٍ يَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَيْهِ سَائِرُ الْأَفْعَالِ فَلَا يَكُونُ الْإِتْيَانُ بِهِ عَلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ الْوَجْهِ سَنَةً وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ بِتَرْكِهِ لِأَنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ وَتَرْكُ السُّنَّةِ لَا يَجِبُ الْجَابِرُ
ترجمہ اور اگر احرام باندھنے والا مکہ میں داخل نہ ہوا اور عرفات کی طرف جا کر وہاں وقوف کیا جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے تو اس سے طواف قدوم ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ طواف قدوم ابتدائے حج میں اس طرح مشروع ہے کہ تمام افعال حج اس پر مرتب ہوں۔ پس اس طریقہ کے علاوہ پر طواف قدوم کو لانا سنت نہ ہو گا۔ اور اس پر اس کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے کچھ واجب بھی نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے اور ترک سنت کی وجہ سے جابر یعنی نقصان کی تلافی کرنے والا واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح اس فصل میں چند متفرق مسائل کا ذکر ہے۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محرم اگر مکہ میں داخل نہ ہوا اور عرفات کے میدان میں چلا گیا اور شریعت کے بیان کردہ طریقہ کے مطابق وہاں وقوف بھی کر لیا تو اس کے ذمہ سے طواف قدوم ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ طواف قدوم ابتدائے حج میں اس طور پر مشروع ہے کہ تمام افعال حج اس پر مرتب ہوں پس اس طریقہ کے علاوہ طواف قدوم سنت نہ ہوگا۔ اور طواف قدوم چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے دم وغیرہ کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے۔ اور ترک سنت سے دم وغیرہ کوئی تلافی کرنے والی چیز واجب نہیں ہوئی۔
Section: And if the Muhrim does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat and makes Wuquf there in the manner we have explained, then Tawaf al-Qudoom is dropped from him because it was prescribed at the beginning of Hajj in a way that the other acts are arranged upon it. So performing it in a manner other than that is not a Sunnah, and there is nothing upon him for omitting it because it is a Sunnah, and the omission of a Sunnah does not require compensation.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining that if a Muhrim goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah and performs Wuquf, the Tawaf al-Qudoom (the initial circumambulation upon arrival) is no longer required. The reason is that Tawaf al-Qudoom is prescribed specifically to precede the other acts of Hajj in Makkah; if one does not enter Makkah first, performing it later would not fulfill that purpose. The passage further clarifies that Tawaf al-Qudoom is a Sunnah, not a Wajib, so omitting it does not necessitate any compensatory act (like offering a dam). The Urdu commentary expands on this, emphasizing that leaving a Sunnah does not require a compensation (jabir). This is a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the sequence of Hajj rituals.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudoom): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Makkah for Hajj or Umrah.
سنة (Sunnah): A recommended act that is not obligatory; omitting it does not require compensation.
جابر (Jabir): A compensatory act required to make up for a deficiency in worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is dropped and a dam is required.
B) It remains recommended but not dropped.
C) It is dropped and no compensation is required.
D) It becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudoom is Sunnah; omitting it when going directly to Arafat requires no compensation.

Sufficiency of Brief Wuquf After Zawal - Hanafi vs Maliki
Hanafi ruling that brief Wuquf after Zawal suffices, rebuttal to Maliki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sufficiency of brief Wuquf after Zawal and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Maliki argument using the word 'aw'.

Core Idea
A brief Wuquf after Zawal suffices because 'aw' in the hadith indicates choice, not a need for both day and night.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends its position that a short stay at Arafat after midday is sufficient for Hajj, even if the pilgrim departs immediately. The Maliki school argues that one must remain until after sunset, covering part of the night. The Hanafi response hinges on the Arabic word 'aw' (or), which grammatically indicates a choice between options. Understanding this linguistic nuance is key to grasping the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State what the Hanafi school says about a pilgrim who makes Wuquf after Zawal and then leaves immediately. Is it valid?
The ruling: it suffices (ajzāhu).
2
Extract the Hanafi proof
Find the hadith cited and the specific word ('aw') that the Hanafis use as evidence. Understand why this word is crucial.
Hadith: 'Whoever makes Wuquf at Arafah for an hour of night or day, his Hajj is complete.' The word 'aw' is key.
3
State the Maliki position and proof
What does Imam Malik require, and what is his evidence?
Malik requires Wuquf in both day and part of night; his proof is a different hadith about catching Arafah at night.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
How do the Hanafis respond to the Maliki argument? Focus on the linguistic point about 'aw' (takhyir – choice).
The Hanafis say that 'aw' gives a choice, so one part (day OR night) is enough. The Maliki hadith sets the end time, not a condition.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
What is the difference in practice between the two schools regarding departure from Arafat?
Hanafi: can leave immediately after Zawal; Maliki: must stay until after sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ إِذَا وَقَفَ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ وَأَفَاضَ مِنْ سَاعَتِهِ أَجْزَاهُ عِنْدَنَا لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ذَكَرَ بِكَلِمَةٍ أَوْ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ الْحَجُّ عَرَفَةُ فَمَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ سَاعَةً مِنْ لَيْلٍ أَوْ نَهَارٍ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَجُّهُ وَهِيَ كَلِمَةُ التَّخْيِيرِ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ لَا يُجْزِيهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَقِفَ فِي الْيَوْمِ وَجُزْءٍ مِّنَ اللَّيْلِ وَلَكِنَّ الْحُجَّةَ عَلَيْهِ مَا رَوَيْنَاهُ
ترجمہ پھر جب زوال کے بعد حاجی نے وقوف عرفہ کیا اور اسی وقت چلا گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کو کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ حضور نے کلمہ او (أو) سے ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حج عرفہ کا نام ہے پس جس نے رات یا دن میں ایک ساعت وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا اور لفظ او کلمہ تخیر ہے اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ کافی نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ دن میں اور رات کے ایک جز میں وقوف کرے لیکن ان کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک یوم عرفہ میں زوال آفتاب کے بعد اگر تھوڑی دیر کا وقوف کیا اور روانہ ہو گیا تو جائز ہے۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ دن میں اور رات کے ایک حصہ میں وقوف ضروری ہے گویا امام مالک کے نزدیک یوم عرفہ میں غروب کے بعد روانہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ امام مالک کا استدلال یہ حدیث ہے من أدرك عرفة بليل فقد أدرك الحج ومن فاته عرفة بليل فقد فاته الحج
Then when he makes Wuquf after Zawal and departs immediately, it suffices for him according to us because the Prophet (peace be upon him) mentioned it with the word 'or', for he said: 'Hajj is Arafah, so whoever makes Wuquf at Arafah for an hour of night or day, his Hajj is complete.' And it is the word of choice. And Malik said: It does not suffice unless he stays during the day and a part of the night. But the proof against him is what we have narrated.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage continues the inter-madhhab dispute, now addressing whether a brief Wuquf after Zawal followed by immediate departure is sufficient. The Hanafi school says yes, because the hadith uses the word 'aw' (or), which indicates that Wuquf can be either during the day or night, not necessarily both. Therefore, even a short stay after Zawal (which is daytime) is enough. Imam Malik requires that the pilgrim stay until after sunset, covering both day and part of the night. The Hanafi rebuttal relies on the explicit hadith with the word 'aw' which is a word of choice, meaning one part is sufficient. The Urdu commentary explains that Malik's evidence (the hadith about catching Arafah at night) is not a counterproof because it sets the end time, not a requirement of staying into the night.

Key Terms
كلمة التخيير (Kalimat al-Takhyir): The word 'aw' (or) in Arabic, which indicates a choice between two options.
الإفاضة (al-Ifadah): The departure from Arafat after Wuquf, moving towards Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim performs Wuquf at Arafah after Zawal and then immediately departs, what is the ruling?
A) The Hajj is invalid because he did not stay until sunset.
B) The Hajj is valid and sufficient because 'aw' indicates one part is enough.
C) He must offer a dam for leaving early.
D) He must return and stay until Fajr the next day.

Key Takeaway
A brief Wuquf at Arafat after Zawal suffices for Hajj according to the Hanafi school, based on the explicit choice indicated by 'aw' in the hadith.

Timing of Wuquf at Arafah: Hanafi vs Maliki
Explains start and end time for Wuquf Arafah and disputes Malik's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the starting time of Wuquf at Arafah and explain the difference with the Maliki view, citing the respective proofs.

Core Idea
Prophetic practice after zawal specifies the start of Wuquf, overriding the literal reading of 'nahar'.

The timing of Wuquf at Arafah is a rukn of Hajj, and its validity depends on when it is performed. The Hanafi and Maliki schools differ on the start time. This lesson examines the proof from prophetic action and hadith to see how the Hanafi school establishes that Wuquf begins after zawal and continues until dawn of the 10th.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim and proofs
Read the passage to find the Hanafi position: Wuquf time starts after zawal on the 9th. Note the two proofs: the Prophet's action (he performed Wuquf after zawal) and the hadith about catching Arafah at night.
The Hanafi proofs are both fi'li (action) and qawli (saying).
2
Identify the Maliki claim and proof
Find Imam Malik's view: Wuquf time begins at dawn or sunrise. Note his proof: the hadith 'al-Hajj Arafah' with the word 'nahar' (day).
Malik relies on the apparent meaning of 'nahar'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
See how Hanafis rebut the Maliki proof: the Prophet's action limits the general term; if earlier time were allowed, the Prophet would have explained it.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-fi'l bayan li al-mujmal (action clarifies the ambiguous).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a pilgrim who stands at Arafah before zawal has a valid Hajj according to Malik but not according to Hanafis.
This affects actual performance of Hajj for followers of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سو
کا بیان ہے۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس نے عرفہ کو رات میں پایا اس نے حج پایا۔ اور جس کو رات بھی عرفہ نہ ملا تو اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا پس یہ آخر وقت کا بیان ہے۔ اور امام مالک اگر چہ کہتے ہیں کہ اول وقت وقوف عرفہ طلوع فجر یا طلوع آفتاب کے بعد ہے لیکن ان کے یہ کا ہے اور عرفہ فجر یا خلاف اس حدیث سے حجت قائم سے جو ہم نے روایت کی۔
تشریح اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ کا وقت کب سے شروع ہوتا ہے تو ہمارے نزدیک یوم عرفہ کے زوال آفتاب کے بعد سے وقت وقوف عرفہ شروع ہوتا ہے چنانچہ اگر حاجی نے یوم عرفہ کے زوال آفتاب سے لے کر یوم نحر کی طلوع فجر تک کسی وقت میں بھی وقوف کیا تو اس کا حج ادا ہو گیا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے زوال کے بعد ہی وقوف فرمایا ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس عمل سے وقوف عرفہ کے اول وقت کا بیان ہوا۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے رات میں وقوف عرفہ پایا اس نے حج کو پایا اور جس کو رات میں بھی وقوف عرفہ نہیں ملا تو اس کا حج جاتا رہا اس حدیث میں وقوف عرفہ کے آخر وقت کا بیان ہے ان دونوں حدیثوں سے ثابت ہوا کہ وقوف عرفہ کا وقت یوم عرفہ کے زاول آفتاب اور یوم نحر کی طلوع فجر کے درمیان ہے۔
امام مالک کا قول یہ ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ کا وقت یوم عرفہ کی طلوع فجر یا طلوع آفتاب کے بعد سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے الحج عرفة فَمَن وقف بعرَفَةَ سَاعَةً مِّنْ لَيْل أو نهار فَقَدَتَمَّ حَجّه یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے حج نام ہے عرفہ کا پس جس نے رات یا دن میں تھوڑی دیر کے لئے عرفہ میں وقوف کیا اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا۔ اس حدیث میں نہار کا لفظ آیا اور ہے اور نہار طلوع شمس سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے وقوف عرفہ کا وقت یوم عرفہ کے طلوع آفتاب سے شروع ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن امام مالک کے خلاف حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عمل حجت ہے کیونکہ آپ نے زوال کے بعد وقوف فرمایا ہے اگر زوال سے پہلے بھی وقت وقوف ہوتا تو آپ اس کا بیان فرماتے ۔
Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 3: It is stated. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever catches Arafah at night has caught the Hajj. And whoever misses Arafah even at night, then his Hajj is lost. So this is an explanation of the last time. And Imam Malik, although he says that the beginning time of Wuquf Arafah is after Fajr or after sunrise, but their this is and Arafah Fajr or against this hadith they establish proof from what we narrated. Explanation: In this regard there is difference: when does the time of Wuquf Arafah begin? In our view, after the decline of the sun (zawal) on the Day of Arafah, the time of Wuquf Arafah begins. So if a pilgrim makes Wuquf at any time from the zawal of the Day of Arafah until the dawn of the Day of Nahr (10th), his Hajj is performed. The proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made Wuquf only after zawal. This action of the Prophet explains the beginning time of Wuquf Arafah. In another hadith, the Prophet said: Whoever catches Wuquf Arafah at night has caught the Hajj, and whoever does not catch Wuquf Arafah at night has lost his Hajj. This hadith explains the last time of Wuquf Arafah. From both hadiths it is proven that the time of Wuquf Arafah is between the zawal of the Day of Arafah and the dawn of the Day of Nahr. Imam Malik's view is that the time of Wuquf Arafah begins after the dawn or after sunrise on the Day of Arafah. Imam Malik's proof is this hadith: 'al-Hajj Arafah, so whoever stands at Arafah for a moment by night or day, his Hajj is complete.' That is, the Prophet said: Hajj is the name of Arafah, so whoever makes Wuquf at Arafah for a short while at night or day, his Hajj is complete. In this hadith, the word 'nahar' (day) appears, and nahar begins from sunrise. Therefore, the time of Wuquf Arafah would begin from sunrise on the Day of Arafah. But against Imam Malik, the action of the Prophet is evidence, because he made Wuquf after zawal. If Wuquf were valid before zawal, he would have explained that.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of Wuquf at Arafah. The Hanafi position, as explained by the commentator, is that the time for Wuquf begins after the sun's decline (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm Arafah) and extends until the dawn of the 10th (Yawm Nahr). This is supported by the Prophet's actual practice – he performed Wuquf after zawal – and by another hadith that considers night-time Wuquf as valid, establishing the end time. Imam Malik holds that the time begins earlier, either at dawn or sunrise on the 9th. His proof is the hadith 'al-Hajj Arafah, so whoever stands at Arafah for a moment by night or day, his Hajj is complete.' He argues that the word 'nahar' (day) means from sunrise. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's own action (Wuquf after zawal) is stronger evidence; if it were permissible before zawal, the Prophet would have done so or explained it. Additionally, the Hanafis interpret the hadith's 'day' as inclusive of the entire period after zawal, as the action specifies the meaning. Thus, the Hanafi position is relied upon.

Key Terms
وقوف عرفہ (Wuquf Arafah): Standing at the plain of Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; a rukn of Hajj.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., declines from the meridian; midday.
یوم عرفہ (Yawm Arafah): The 9th day of Dhul Hijjah.
نہار (nahar): Daytime, from sunrise to sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for Wuquf at Arafah begin?
A) At sunrise on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah
B) At dawn (fajr) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah
C) After zawal (decline of the sun) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah
D) At sunset on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafah is a rukn of Hajj; its valid time according to the Hanafi school is from zawal on the 9th to dawn on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Brief Wuquf After Zawal: Hanafi vs Maliki
Rules that a short stop at Arafah after zawal suffices, contra Malik's requirement of night stay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a brief Wuquf after zawal suffices for Hajj and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using hadith analysis.

Core Idea
A short stop at Arafah after noon suffices; night stay is not required in the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: is a brief Wuquf at Arafah after zawal sufficient, or must one also stay into the night? The Hanafi school relies on a Prophetic hadith using the word 'or' to allow either day or night, while Imam Malik requires a portion of the night. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting textual evidence in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a brief Wuquf after zawal, even without staying into the night, makes Hajj complete.
The key phrase is 'ajzāhu' (it suffices).
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam Malik requires Wuquf in both the day and a part of the night; departing before sunset invalidates Hajj.
Malik uses a hadith emphasizing night-time.
3
Trace the Maliki proof
Mālik's ḥadīth: 'Whoever catches Arafah by night has caught the Hajj...' – this makes night essential.
This hadith is his mustadil.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that Mālik's version with 'night' is not well-known (ghayr mashhūr); the authentic version is: 'Whoever catches Arafah has caught the Hajj'. The Hanafi proof uses 'al-Ḥajj Arafah … by night or day' – the word 'or' gives choice.
Thus, day-only Wuquf is sufficient.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if a pilgrim makes Wuquf after zawal and leaves before sunset, it is valid according to Hanafis but invalid according to Mālik.
This difference affects real Hajj performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زوال کے بعد تھوڑی دیر وقوف عرفہ کر کے کوچ کرے تو کیا حکم ہے
ثُمَّ إِذَا وَقَفَ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ وَافَاضَ مِنْ سَاعَتِهِ أَجْزَاهُ عِندَنَا لا لَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ذَكَرَ بِكَلِمَةٍ أَوْ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ الْحَج عَرَفَةٌ فَمَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةٍ سَاعَةً مِنْ لَيْل أَوْنَهَارِ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَبُّهُ وَهِيَ كَلِمَةُ التَّخَيْرِ وَ قَالَ مَالِكٌ لَا يُجْزِيهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَقِفَ فِي اليَوْمِ وَجُزْءٌ مِّنَ اللَّيْلِ وَلكِنْ الحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا رَوَيْنَاهُ
ترجمہ پھر جب زوال کے بعد حاجی نے وقوف عرفہ کیا اور اسی وقت چلا گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کو کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ حضور نے کلمہ اوذ کر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ آپ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حج عرفہ کا نام ہے پس جس نے رات یا دن میں ایک ساعت وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا اور لفظ او کلمہ تخیر ہے اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ کافی نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ دن میں اور رات کے ایک جز میں وقوف کرے لیکن ان کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک یوم عرفہ میں زوال آفتاب کے بعد اگر تھوڑی دیر کا وقوف کیا اور روانہ ہو گیا تو جائز ہے۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ دن میں اور رات کے ایک حصہ میں وقوف ضروری ہے گویا امام مالک کے نزدیک یوم عرفہ میں غروب کے بعد روانہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ امام مالک کا ستدل یہ حدیت ہے من أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَةَ بِلَيْلِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَ مَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَةَ بِلَيلِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ
اس حدیث میں حج کا دارو مدار رات میں وقوف عرفہ پر ہے۔ اس لئے امام مالک نے کہا کہ رات کے ایک حصہ میں وقوف کرنا ضروری ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان الْحَج عرفةُ فَمَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ سَاعَةً مِّنْ لَيْلٍ أَوْ نَهَارٍ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حجہ میں کلمہ او خیر کے لئے ہے یعنی وقوف دن میں کرے یا رات میں کرے دونوں صورتوں میں حج پورا ہو جائے گا۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ وقوف کے لئے نہ دن کی شرط ہے اور نہ رات کی ۔ یہی حدیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہوگی ۔ امام مالک کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث میں بیل کی زیادتی غیر مشہور ہے۔ مشہور تو فقط یہ ہے مَنْ أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَةَ فَقَدْ أدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَ مَنْ فَاتَ عَرَفَةَ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجِّ ہذا یہ حدیث امام مالک کا مستدل نہ ہو سکے گی۔
What is the ruling if he makes Wuquf after zawal and departs immediately? Then if he stands after zawal and moves on from that very hour, it suffices for him according to us, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) mentioned the word 'or'. Indeed he said: 'Hajj is Arafah. So whoever stands at Arafah for an hour by night or day, his Hajj is complete.' And it is a word of choice. And Malik said: It does not suffice him unless he stands in the day and a part of the night. But the proof against him is what we narrated. Translation: Then when the pilgrim makes Wuquf Arafah after zawal and leaves at that time, it is sufficient according to us, because the Prophet used the word 'or'. Because he said that Hajj is the name of Arafah, so whoever makes Wuquf Arafah for one hour by night or day, his Hajj is complete, and the word 'or' indicates choice. And Imam Malik said that it is not sufficient unless he makes Wuquf in the day and a part of the night. But against him, the hadith we narrated is proof. Explanation: The issue is that in our view, on the Day of Arafah after zawal, if he makes a brief Wuquf and leaves, it is permissible. Imam Malik ruled that Wuquf in the day and a part of the night is necessary; meaning that in his view, departing after sunset on the Day of Arafah is necessary. Imam Malik's evidence is this hadith: 'Whoever catches Arafah by night has caught the Hajj, and whoever misses Arafah by night has missed it.' In this hadith, the entire Hajj depends on night-time Wuquf. Therefore, Malik said that Wuquf in a part of the night is necessary. Our proof is that in the Prophet's saying 'al-Hajj Arafah, so whoever stands at Arafah for an hour by night or day, his Hajj is complete,' the word 'or' indicates choice, meaning whether he makes Wuquf during the day or night, in both cases his Hajj is complete. Thus it is known that for Wuquf, neither day nor night is a condition. This same hadith will be proof against Imam Malik. The version of the hadith presented by Imam Malik with the addition of 'night' is not well-known. The well-known version is only: 'Whoever catches Arafah has caught the Hajj, and whoever misses Arafah has missed the Hajj.' Thus this hadith cannot be evidence for Imam Malik.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents another inter-madhhab dispute, specifically whether a brief Wuquf after zawal followed by immediate departure is sufficient. The Hanafi position is that it is sufficient, based on the hadith 'al-Hajj Arafah... by night or day,' where the word 'or' gives a choice between day and night; thus either is valid without requiring both. The commentator explains that Imam Malik requires Wuquf in both day and a part of the night, based on a different hadith that emphasizes night-time. The Hanafi response is that the hadith Malik uses includes an addition ('night') that is not widely authentic; the well-known version does not specify night. Therefore, the Hanafi view prevails: a short Wuquf after zawal is valid, and one may depart immediately without waiting for night.

Key Terms
کلمہ تخیر (kalimat al-takhyir): A word indicating choice, here 'aw' (or) in the hadith.
مستدل (mustadil): Evidence or proof used by a scholar to support his position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim makes Wuquf at Arafah for a short time after zawal and then leaves immediately, his Hajj is:
A) Invalid because he did not stay until night
B) Valid because the hadith allows either day or night
C) Valid only if he also spends the night at Muzdalifah
D) Invalid because he must stay until sunset

Key Takeaway
A brief Wuquf at Arafah after zawal suffices for Hajj in the Hanafi school because the authentic hadith gives a choice between day and night, and the Maliki requirement of night stay is based on a less authentic narration.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Wuquf Valid While Asleep, Unconscious, or Unaware
Rules that Wuquf is valid even if one passes through Arafah asleep, unconscious, or unaware

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wuquf when the pilgrim is unconscious or unaware and apply the analogy to fasting.

Core Idea
Wuquf is valid by mere presence; intention and awareness are not required for this rukn.

You might think that for any act of worship, you need to be conscious and intend it. However, the Hanafi school holds that wuquf (standing at Arafah) is a rukn that is fulfilled by physical presence alone. This lesson examines the ruling and the reasoning behind it, drawing an analogy to fasting and contrasting with prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is wuquf at Arafah. The ruling: it is valid (jaza) even if the pilgrim is asleep, unconscious, or unaware of the location.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is qiyas (analogy) with the rukn of fasting. The author compares wuquf to fasting: both are valid even if the person is unconscious or asleep, because the essential rukn (presence in Arafah or abstention in fasting) is present.
The distinction from prayer shows that prayer requires continuous awareness, so its rukn is different.
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The illa for the ruling is that the rukn of wuquf is mere presence, not intention or awareness. Similarly, the rukn of fasting is abstention, which does not require consciousness. Intention is a condition only for acts that require continuous awareness, like prayer.
The passage explicitly states: 'ignorance causes defect in intention, and intention is not a condition for every rukn.'
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) might require intention for wuquf. The Hanafi school rejects this because intention is not a condition for this particular rukn. The practical consequence: a pilgrim who passes through Arafah unconsciously still fulfills the rukn.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالت نیند یا بے ہوشی کی حالت میں میدان عرفات سے گذرا تو فرض ادا ہو جائے گا
وَمَنْ أَجْتَازَ بِعَرَفَةَ نَائِمًا أَوْ مُعْتَى عَلَيْهِ أَوْ لَا يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهَا عَرَفَاتُ جَازَ عَنِ الْوُقُوفِ لِأَنَّ مَا هُوَ الرُّكُنُ وَقَدْ وُجِدَ وَهُوَ الوقوف وَلَا يَسْمَعُ ذَلِكَ بِالْاِعْمَاءِ وَ النَّوْمِ كَرُكْنِ الصَّوْمِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّلوةِ لأَنَّهَا لَا تَبْقَى مَعَ الْإِغْمَاءِ وَالْجَهلُ يُحِلُّ بِالبَيَةِ وَهِيَ لَيْسَتْ بِشَرُطٍ لِكُلِّ رُكَن
ترجمہ اور جو شخص عرفہ سے گذرا اس حال میں کہ وہ سو یا ہوا بنے یا بے ہوش ہے یا اس کو اس کی خبر نہ ہوئی کہ یہ عرفات ہے تو وقوف جائز ہوگا کیونکہ جور کن ہے وہ پایا گیا اورہ کن وقوف ہے اور اغماء اور نوم کی وجہ سے یہ منع نہیں ہوگا جیسے رکن صوم ہے برخلاف نماز کے کیونکہ نماز تو انما ، کے ساتھ باقی نہیں رہتی ہے۔ اور جہل نیت میں خلل پیدا کرتا ہے اور نیت ہر رکن کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک حاجی سوتا ہوا یا بے ہوشی کی حالت میں عرفات سے عرفہ کے دن گذرا چلا گیا یا اس کو یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ جہاں سے میں گذر رہا ہوں یہی عرفات ہے۔ ان تینوں صورتوں میں وقوف عرفہ ادا ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ حج کا رکن وقوف ہے اور وہ پایا گیا۔ اور رہا اغماء اور سونا تو وہ وقوف کے لئے مانع نہیں ہیں جیسے کسی نے اول صبح میں روزے کی نیت کی پھر دن بھر سوتا رہا یا بے ہوش پڑا رہا تو اس کا روزہ ادا ہو گیا۔ برخلاف نماز کے کیونکہ نماز اغماء کے ساتھ باقی نہیں رہتی ہے اور ربا عرفات کا علم نہ ہونا تو یہ نہ جاننا نیت میں خلل پیدا کرتا ہے یعنی جس چیز کا علم نہ ہو اس کی نیست معتبر نہیں ہے۔ لیکن ہر رکن کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے لہذا وقوف کے لئے بھی نیت شرط نہ ہوگی اور جب نیت شرط نہیں تو عرفات کو جانے بغیر اس سے گذرنا وقوف شمار ہوگا۔
If one passes through Arafah while sleeping or unconscious or does not know that it is Arafat, it is valid as Wuquf. Because the rukn that is present is the Wuquf, and this is not prevented by unconsciousness and sleep, like the rukn of fasting, unlike prayer because prayer does not remain with unconsciousness. And ignorance causes defect in intention, and intention is not a condition for every rukn. Translation: And a person who passed through Arafah while sleeping or unconscious or he did not know that these are Arafat, then the Wuquf is valid because the rukn that is present is the Wuquf, and unconsciousness and sleep do not prevent this, like the rukn of fasting, unlike prayer because prayer does not remain with unconsciousness. And ignorance creates a defect in intention, and intention is not a condition for every rukn. Explanation: The case is that a pilgrim passes through Arafat while sleeping or in a state of unconsciousness on the Day of Arafah, or he does not know that the place he is passing through is Arafat. In all three cases, the Wuquf Arafah is performed. Because the rukn of Hajj is Wuquf, and it is present. As for unconsciousness and sleep, they are not obstacles for Wuquf, just as if someone made intention for fasting at the beginning of the morning and then slept the whole day or remained unconscious, his fasting is valid. Unlike prayer, because prayer does not remain with unconsciousness. And not knowing Arafat: this ignorance causes a defect in intention, but intention is not a condition for every rukn. Therefore, Wuquf is valid even without intention.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This lesson presents a Hanafi ruling on the validity of Wuquf when a person passes through Arafah in a state of sleep, unconsciousness, or ignorance. The ruling is that Wuquf is valid because it is a rukn that is fulfilled by mere presence; consciousness and intention are not required for this rukn. The commentator provides an analogy with fasting: fasting remains valid even if one sleeps the whole day or is unconscious, because the rukn (abstention) is present. The ruling is contrasted with prayer, which is invalidated by unconsciousness because prayer requires continuous awareness. As for ignorance, it affects intention, but since intention is not a condition for Wuquf (unlike for prayer or purification), ignorance does not invalidate it. Thus, the Hanafi school emphasizes the physical presence as the essence of Wuquf.

Key Terms
رکن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of Hajj; its omission invalidates the act.
اغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness; a state that does not affect the validity of certain acts like fasting or wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim passes through Arafah while unconscious, his Wuquf is:
A) Invalid because he was not aware
B) Valid because the rukn of presence is fulfilled
C) Valid only if someone intended on his behalf
D) Invalid because unconsciousness invalidates all acts

Key Takeaway
The rukn of wuquf is fulfilled by physical presence in Arafah, regardless of consciousness or intention.
